Empire, in the eastern Mediterranean, continued as what came to be called the Byzantine Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger200197,_103_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger200197,_103-160">[156]</a></sup> Centuries later, a limited unity would be restored to western Europe through the establishment in 962 of a revived "Roman Empire",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollins1999404_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollins1999404-161">[157]</a></sup> later called the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELoyn1991122–123_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELoyn1991122–123-162">[158]</a></sup> comprising a number of states in what is now Germany, Austria, Switzerland, Czech Republic, Belgium, Italy, and parts of France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJohnson199623_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJohnson199623-164">[160]</a></sup>
</p><p>In China, <a href="/wiki/Dynasty" title="Dynasty">dynasties</a> would rise and fall, but, by sharp contrast to the Mediterranean-European world, dynastic unity would be restored. After the fall of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Han_dynasty" title="Eastern Han dynasty">Eastern Han dynasty</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[161]</a></sup> and the demise of the Three Kingdoms, <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomadic</a> tribes from the north began to invade in the 4th century, eventually conquering areas of northern China and setting up many small kingdoms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[162]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sui_dynasty" title="Sui dynasty">Sui dynasty</a> successfully reunified the whole of China<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGascoigne200390–92_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGascoigne200390–92-167">[163]</a></sup> in 581,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGernet1996237–238_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGernet1996237–238-168">[164]</a></sup> and laid the foundations for a Chinese golden age under the <a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty" title="Tang dynasty">Tang dynasty</a> (618–907).
</p>
<h2><span id="Post-classical_history_.28476.E2.80.931450.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-classical_history_(476–1450)">Post-classical history (476–1450)</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Post-classical_history" title="Post-classical history">Post-classical history</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sankore_Moske_Timboektoe.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="960" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Sankore_Moske_Timboektoe.JPG/220px-Sankore_Moske_Timboektoe.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Sankore_Moske_Timboektoe.JPG/330px-Sankore_Moske_Timboektoe.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Sankore_Moske_Timboektoe.JPG/440px-Sankore_Moske_Timboektoe.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sankore_Moske_Timboektoe.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/University_of_Timbuktu" title="University of Timbuktu">University of Timbuktu</a>, Mali</div></div></div>
<p>The term "post-classical era", though derived from the name of the era of "<a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical antiquity</a>", takes in a broader geographic sweep.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStearns201796_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStearns201796-169">[165]</a></sup> The era is commonly dated from the 5th century <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Western_Roman_Empire" title="Fall of the Western Roman Empire">fall of the Western Roman Empire</a>, which fragmented into many separate kingdoms, some of which would later be confederated under the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>. The Byzantine Empire survived until late in the post-classical or medieval period.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hagia_Sophia_Mars_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3681" data-file-width="5514" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Hagia_Sophia_Mars_2013.jpg/220px-Hagia_Sophia_Mars_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Hagia_Sophia_Mars_2013.jpg/330px-Hagia_Sophia_Mars_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Hagia_Sophia_Mars_2013.jpg/440px-Hagia_Sophia_Mars_2013.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hagia_Sophia_Mars_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hagia_Sophia" title="Hagia Sophia">Hagia Sophia</a>, in Istanbul, is among the most recognizable symbols of the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire#Culture" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine civilization</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BAT_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-BAT-170">[166]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The post-classical period also encompasses the <a href="/wiki/Early_Muslim_conquests" title="Early Muslim conquests">Early Muslim conquests</a>, the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">Islamic Golden Age</a>, and the commencement and expansion of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_slave_trade" title="Arab slave trade">Arab slave trade</a>, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_and_conquests" title="Mongol invasions and conquests">Mongol invasions</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a> and the founding around 1280 of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShaw197613_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShaw197613-171">[167]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a> saw a series of <a href="/wiki/Middle_kingdoms_of_India" title="Middle kingdoms of India">middle kingdoms of India</a>, followed by the establishment of <a href="/wiki/Islamic_rulers_in_the_Indian_subcontinent" title="Islamic rulers in the Indian subcontinent">Islamic empires in India</a>.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mali_Empire" title="Mali Empire">Mali Empire</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Songhai_Empire" title="Songhai Empire">Songhai Empire</a> rose.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015379,_393_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015379,_393-172">[168]</a></sup> On the southeast coast of Africa, Arabic ports were established where <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spice_trade" title="Spice trade">spices</a>, and other commodities were traded. This allowed Africa to join the <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> trading system, bringing it contact with Asia; this, along with Muslim culture, resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Swahili_culture" title="Swahili culture">Swahili culture</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> experienced the successive <a href="/wiki/Sui_dynasty" title="Sui dynasty">Sui</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty" title="Tang dynasty">Tang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Song_dynasty" title="Song dynasty">Song</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yuan_dynasty" title="Yuan dynasty">Yuan</a>, and early <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming</a> dynasties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015297,_336,_339_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015297,_336,_339-173">[169]</a></sup> Middle Eastern trade routes along the Indian Ocean, and the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> through the <a href="/wiki/Gobi_Desert" title="Gobi Desert">Gobi Desert</a>, provided limited economic and cultural contact between Asian and European civilizations.
</p><p>During the same period, civilizations in the Americas, such as the <a href="/wiki/Mississippian_culture" title="Mississippian culture">Mississippians</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015214_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015214-174">[170]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ancestral_Puebloans" title="Ancestral Puebloans">Puebloans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aztec_Empire" title="Aztec Empire">Aztecs</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015395_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015395-175">[171]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Maya_civilization" title="Maya civilization">Maya</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015205_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015205-176">[172]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Muisca_Confederation" title="Muisca Confederation">Muisca</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Inca_Empire" title="Inca Empire">Inca</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015397_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015397-177">[173]</a></sup> reached their zenith. All would be compromised by, then conquered after, contact with <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">European colonists</a> at the beginning of the modern period.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greater_Middle_East">Greater Middle East</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Middle_East" title="History of the Middle East">History of the Middle East</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_North_Africa" title="History of North Africa">History of North Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Central_Asia" title="History of Central Asia">History of Central Asia</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Caucasus" title="History of the Caucasus">History of the Caucasus</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">Islamic Golden Age</a></div>
<p>Prior to the advent of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> in the 7th century, the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> was dominated by the Byzantine Empire and the <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Empire" title="Sasanian Empire">Sasanian Empire</a> that frequently fought each other for control of several disputed regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHourani19915,_11_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHourani19915,_11-178">[174]</a></sup> This was also a cultural battle, with Byzantine <a href="/wiki/Christian_culture" title="Christian culture">Christian culture</a> competing against Persian <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrian</a> traditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015249–50_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015249–50-179">[175]</a></sup> The birth of <a href="/wiki/History_of_Islam" title="History of Islam">Islam</a> created a new contender that quickly surpassed both of these empires. The new religion greatly affected the <a href="/wiki/Political_history" title="Political history">political</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economic_history" title="Economic history">economic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Military_history" title="Military history">military history</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Old_World" title="Old World">Old World</a>, especially the Middle East.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grande_Mosqu%C3%A9e_de_Kairouan,_vue_d%27ensemble.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3551" data-file-width="4620" decoding="async" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Grande_Mosqu%C3%A9e_de_Kairouan%2C_vue_d%27ensemble.jpg/220px-Grande_Mosqu%C3%A9e_de_Kairouan%2C_vue_d%27ensemble.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Grande_Mosqu%C3%A9e_de_Kairouan%2C_vue_d%27ensemble.jpg/330px-Grande_Mosqu%C3%A9e_de_Kairouan%2C_vue_d%27ensemble.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Grande_Mosqu%C3%A9e_de_Kairouan%2C_vue_d%27ensemble.jpg/440px-Grande_Mosqu%C3%A9e_de_Kairouan%2C_vue_d%27ensemble.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Grande_Mosqu%C3%A9e_de_Kairouan,_vue_d%27ensemble.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Great_Mosque_of_Kairouan" title="Great Mosque of Kairouan">Great Mosque of Kairouan</a>, Tunisia, founded 670 CE</div></div></div>
<p>From their center on the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">Arabian Peninsula</a>, Muslims began their expansion during the early post-classical era. By 750 CE, they came to conquer most of the Near East, North Africa, and parts of Europe,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015255_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015255-180">[176]</a></sup> ushering in an era of learning, science, and invention known as the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">Islamic Golden Age</a>. The knowledge and skills of the ancient Near East, Greece, and Persia were preserved in the post-classical era by Muslims, who also added new and important innovations from outside, such as the manufacture of paper from China and decimal positional numbering from India.
</p><p>Much of this learning and development can be linked to geography. Even prior to Islam's presence, the city of <a href="/wiki/Mecca" title="Mecca">Mecca</a> had served as a center of trade in Arabia, and the Islamic prophet <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a> himself was a merchant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015251_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015251-181">[177]</a></sup> With the new Islamic tradition of the <i><a href="/wiki/Hajj" title="Hajj">Hajj</a></i>, the pilgrimage to Mecca, the city became even more a center for exchanging goods and ideas. The influence held by Muslim merchants over African-Arabian and Arabian-Asian trade routes was tremendous. As a result, Islamic civilization grew and expanded on the basis of its merchant economy, in contrast to the Europeans, Indians, and Chinese, who based their societies on an agricultural landholding nobility. Merchants brought goods and their Islamic faith to <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_China" title="Islam in China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_India" title="Islam in India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Southeast_Asia" title="Islam in Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Africa" title="Islam in Africa">Africa</a>, and returned with new discoveries and inventions.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Crac_des_chevaliers_syria.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1566" data-file-width="4015" decoding="async" height="86" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Crac_des_chevaliers_syria.jpeg/220px-Crac_des_chevaliers_syria.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Crac_des_chevaliers_syria.jpeg/330px-Crac_des_chevaliers_syria.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Crac_des_chevaliers_syria.jpeg/440px-Crac_des_chevaliers_syria.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Crac_des_chevaliers_syria.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Crusading_movement" title="Crusading movement">Crusader</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Krak_des_Chevaliers" title="Krak des Chevaliers">Krak des Chevaliers</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Crusading_movement" title="Crusading movement">Crusading movement</a> was a religiously motivated European effort to roll back Muslim territory and regain control of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Land" title="Holy Land">Holy Land</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015292–93_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015292–93-182">[178]</a></sup> It was ultimately unsuccessful and served more to weaken the Byzantine Empire, especially with the 1204 <a href="/wiki/Sack_of_Constantinople" title="Sack of Constantinople">Sack of Constantinople</a>. Arab domination of the region ended in the mid-11th century with the arrival of the <a href="/wiki/Seljuk_dynasty" title="Seljuk dynasty">Seljuk Turks</a>, migrating south from the Turkic homelands. In the early 13th century, a new wave of invaders, the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol Empire</a>, swept through the region but were eventually eclipsed by the Turks and the founding of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> around 1280.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShaw197613_171-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShaw197613-171">[167]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a> saw the rise of polities established by the <a href="/wiki/Berbers" title="Berbers">Berbers</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Marinid_Sultanate" title="Marinid Sultanate">Marinid dynasty</a> in <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Zayyanid_dynasty" title="Zayyanid dynasty">Zayyanid dynasty</a> in <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Hafsid_dynasty" title="Hafsid dynasty">Hafsid dynasty</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>. The coastal region was known as the <a href="/wiki/Barbary_Coast" title="Barbary Coast">Barbary Coast</a>. Pirates based in North African ports conducted operations that included capturing merchant ships and raiding coastal settlements. Many European captives were sold in North African markets as part of the <a href="/wiki/Barbary_slave_trade" title="Barbary slave trade">Barbary slave trade</a>.
</p><p>Starting with the <a href="/wiki/Sui_dynasty" title="Sui dynasty">Sui dynasty</a> (581–618), the Chinese began expanding to the west. They were confronted by <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic</a> nomads, who were becoming the most dominant ethnic group in <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEbreyWalthallPalais2006113_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEbreyWalthallPalais2006113-183">[179]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEXue1992149–152,_257–264_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEXue1992149–152,_257–264-184">[180]</a></sup> Originally the relationship was largely cooperative but in 630, the <a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty" title="Tang dynasty">Tang dynasty</a> began an offensive against the Turks by capturing areas of the <a href="/wiki/Ordos_Desert" title="Ordos Desert">Ordos Desert</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEXue1992226–227_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEXue1992226–227-185">[181]</a></sup> In the 8th century, Islam began to penetrate the region and soon became the sole faith of most of the population, though Buddhism remained strong in the east.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[182]</a></sup> The desert nomads of <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">Arabia</a> could militarily match the nomads of the steppe, and the <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">Umayyad Caliphate</a> gained control over parts of Central Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEbreyWalthallPalais2006113_183-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEbreyWalthallPalais2006113-183">[179]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Hephthalites" title="Hephthalites">Hephthalites</a> were the most powerful of the nomad groups in the 6th and 7th centuries, and controlled much of the region. From the 9th to 13th centuries, the region was divided among several powerful states, including the <a href="/wiki/Samanid_Empire" title="Samanid Empire">Samanid Empire</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[183]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Seljuk_Empire" title="Seljuk Empire">Seljuk Empire</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEṬabībFaḍlallāhNishapuriNīšāpūrī20019_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEṬabībFaḍlallāhNishapuriNīšāpūrī20019-188">[184]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Khwarazmian_Empire" title="Khwarazmian Empire">Khwarazmian Empire</a>. The largest empire to rise out of Central Asia developed when <a href="/wiki/Genghis_Khan" title="Genghis Khan">Genghis Khan</a> united the tribes of Mongolia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillMcNeill2003120_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillMcNeill2003120-189">[185]</a></sup> The Mongol Empire spread to comprise all of Central Asia and China as well as large parts of Russia and the Middle East.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[186]</a></sup> After Genghis Khan died in 1227,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger2001153_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger2001153-191">[187]</a></sup> most of Central Asia continued to be dominated by a successor state, the <a href="/wiki/Chagatai_Khanate" title="Chagatai Khanate">Chagatai Khanate</a>. In 1369, <a href="/wiki/Timur" title="Timur">Timur</a>, a Turkic leader in the Mongol military tradition, conquered most of the region and founded the <a href="/wiki/Timurid_Empire" title="Timurid Empire">Timurid Empire</a>. However, Timur's large empire collapsed soon after his death as much of Central Asia was overrun by the <a href="/wiki/Uzbeks" title="Uzbeks">Uzbeks</a>.
</p><p>In the aftermath of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Byzantine%E2%80%93Sasanian_wars" title="Byzantine–Sasanian wars">Byzantine–Sasanian wars</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Peoples_of_the_Caucasus" title="Peoples of the Caucasus">diverse group of peoples</a> gained freedom from foreign suzerainty. As the Byzantines and Sasanians became exhausted due to continuous wars, the <a href="/wiki/Rashidun_Caliphate" title="Rashidun Caliphate">Rashidun Caliphate</a> had the opportunity to expand into the Caucasus during the <a href="/wiki/Early_Muslim_conquests" title="Early Muslim conquests">early Muslim conquests</a>. By the 13th century, the arrival of the Mongols saw the region invaded once again.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Europe" title="History of Europe">History of Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christendom" title="Christendom">Christendom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_Middle_Ages" title="Timeline of the Middle Ages">Timeline of the Middle Ages</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Saint_Peter%27s_Basilica_facade,_Rome,_Italy.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2975" data-file-width="4470" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Saint_Peter%27s_Basilica_facade%2C_Rome%2C_Italy.jpg/220px-Saint_Peter%27s_Basilica_facade%2C_Rome%2C_Italy.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Saint_Peter%27s_Basilica_facade%2C_Rome%2C_Italy.jpg/330px-Saint_Peter%27s_Basilica_facade%2C_Rome%2C_Italy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Saint_Peter%27s_Basilica_facade%2C_Rome%2C_Italy.jpg/440px-Saint_Peter%27s_Basilica_facade%2C_Rome%2C_Italy.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Saint_Peter%27s_Basilica_facade,_Rome,_Italy.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Basilica" title="St. Peter's Basilica">St. Peter's Basilica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Since at least the 4th century, <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, primarily <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholicism</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[188]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[189]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[190]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[191]</a></sup> and later <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[192]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[193]</a></sup> has played a <a href="/wiki/Role_of_Christianity_in_civilization" title="Role of Christianity in civilization">prominent role</a> in the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Western_civilization" title="History of Western civilization">shaping of Western civilization</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Caltron_J.H_Hayas_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-Caltron_J.H_Hayas-198">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Orlandis_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-Orlandis-199">[195]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-How_The_Catholic_Church_Built_Western_Civilization_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-How_The_Catholic_Church_Built_Western_Civilization-200">[196]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perry2012_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-Perry2012-201">[197]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Early_Middle_Ages" title="Early Middle Ages">Early Middle Ages</a> was characterized by depopulation, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deurbanization" title="Deurbanization">deurbanization</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Barbarian" title="Barbarian">barbarian</a> invasion, all of which had begun in <a href="/wiki/Late_antiquity" title="Late antiquity">late antiquity</a>. The barbarian invaders formed their own new kingdoms in the remains of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a>. In the 7th century, North Africa and the Middle East, once part of the Eastern Roman Empire, became part of the <a href="/wiki/Caliphate" title="Caliphate">Caliphate</a> after conquest by <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a>'s successors. Although there were substantial changes in society and political structures, most of the new kingdoms incorporated as many of the existing Roman institutions as they could. Christianity expanded in western Europe, and monasteries were founded. In the 7th and 8th centuries, the <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Franks</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Carolingian_dynasty" title="Carolingian dynasty">Carolingian dynasty</a> established an empire covering much of <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[198]</a></sup> it lasted until the 9th century, when it succumbed to pressure from new invaders—the <a href="/wiki/Vikings" title="Vikings">Vikings</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[199]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hungarians#Entering_the_Carpathian_Basin_(c._895)" title="Hungarians">Magyars</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saracen" title="Saracen">Saracens</a>.
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/High_Middle_Ages" title="High Middle Ages">High Middle Ages</a>, which began after 1000, the population of Europe increased greatly as technological and agricultural innovations allowed trade to flourish and crop yields to increase. <a href="/wiki/Manorialism" title="Manorialism">Manorialism</a>, the organization of peasants into villages that owed rents and labor service to nobles, and <a href="/wiki/Feudalism" title="Feudalism">feudalism</a>, a political structure whereby <a href="/wiki/Knight" title="Knight">knights</a> and lower-status nobles owed military service to their overlords in return for the right to rents from lands and <a href="/wiki/Manorialism" title="Manorialism">manors</a>, were two of the ways of organizing medieval society that developed during the High Middle Ages. Kingdoms became more centralized after the decentralizing effects of the break-up of the <a href="/wiki/Carolingian_Empire" title="Carolingian Empire">Carolingian Empire</a>. In 1054, the <a href="/wiki/East%E2%80%93West_Schism" title="East–West Schism">Great Schism</a> between the Catholic Church and the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a> led to the prominent cultural differences between Western and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BideleuxJeffries48_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-BideleuxJeffries48-204">[200]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Crusading_movement" title="Crusading movement">Crusading movement</a> attempted to gain Christian control of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Land" title="Holy Land">Holy Land</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a> and succeeded for long enough to establish some <a href="/wiki/Crusader_states" title="Crusader states">Crusader states</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a>. Italian merchants imported slaves to work in households or in <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">sugar</a> processing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[201]</a></sup> Intellectual life was marked by <a href="/wiki/Scholasticism" title="Scholasticism">scholasticism</a> and the founding of universities, while the building of <a href="/wiki/Gothic_cathedrals_and_churches" title="Gothic cathedrals and churches">Gothic cathedrals and churches</a> was one of the outstanding artistic achievements of the age.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillMcNeill2003146_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillMcNeill2003146-206">[202]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Notredame_Paris.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2318" data-file-width="3086" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Notredame_Paris.JPG/220px-Notredame_Paris.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Notredame_Paris.JPG/330px-Notredame_Paris.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Notredame_Paris.JPG/440px-Notredame_Paris.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Notredame_Paris.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Notre-Dame_de_Paris" title="Notre-Dame de Paris">Notre-Dame de Paris</a> in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>: is among the most recognizable symbols of the <a href="/wiki/Role_of_Christianity_in_civilization" title="Role of Christianity in civilization">civilization</a> of <a href="/wiki/Christendom" title="Christendom">Christendom</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Late_Middle_Ages" title="Late Middle Ages">Late Middle Ages</a> were marked by difficulties and calamities. Famine, plague, and war devastated the population of Western Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[203]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a> alone killed approximately 75 to 200 million people between 1347 and 1350.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[204]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[205]</a></sup> It was one of the deadliest pandemics in human history. Starting in Asia, the disease reached the Mediterranean and Western Europe during the late 1340s,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[206]</a></sup> and killed tens of millions of Europeans in six years; between a quarter and a third of the population perished.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillMcNeill2003120_189-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillMcNeill2003120-189">[185]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Middle Ages witnessed the first sustained <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">urbanization</a> of northern and western Europe and it lasted until the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_period" title="Early modern period">early modern period</a> in the 16th century,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBentleyZiegler2008595_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBentleyZiegler2008595-211">[207]</a></sup> marked by the rise of <a href="/wiki/Nation_state" title="Nation state">nation states</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger2001280_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStearnsLanger2001280-212">[208]</a></sup> the division of Western Christianity in the <a href="/wiki/Reformation" title="Reformation">Reformation</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeill1999319–323_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeill1999319–323-213">[209]</a></sup> the rise of <a href="/wiki/Humanism" title="Humanism">humanism</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Renaissance" title="Italian Renaissance">Italian Renaissance</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeill1999267–268_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeill1999267–268-214">[210]</a></sup> and the beginnings of European overseas expansion which allowed for the <a href="/wiki/Columbian_exchange" title="Columbian exchange">Columbian exchange</a>.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central</a> and Eastern Europe, in 1386, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Poland_(1385%E2%80%931569)" title="Kingdom of Poland (1385–1569)">Kingdom of Poland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Grand Duchy of Lithuania</a> (the latter including territories of modern <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>), facing depredations by the <a href="/wiki/State_of_the_Teutonic_Order" title="State of the Teutonic Order">Teutonic Order</a> and later also threats from <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Moscow" title="Grand Duchy of Moscow">Muscovy</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Khanate" title="Crimean Khanate">Crimean Khanate</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, formed a <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a> through the marriage of Poland's Queen <a href="/wiki/Jadwiga_of_Poland" title="Jadwiga of Poland">Jadwiga</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_rulers_of_Lithuania" title="List of rulers of Lithuania">Lithuanian Grand Duke</a> Jogaila, who became King <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_II_Jagie%C5%82%C5%82o" title="Władysław II Jagiełło">Władysław II Jagiełło</a> of Poland. For the next four centuries, until the 18th-century <a href="/wiki/Partitions_of_Poland" title="Partitions of Poland">partitions of the Polish-Lithuanian Commonwealth</a> by <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, the two polities conducted a federated <a href="/wiki/Condominium_(international_law)" title="Condominium (international law)">condominium</a>, long Europe's largest state, which welcomed diverse ethnicities and religions, including most of the world's <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>, furthered scientific thought (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Nicolaus_Copernicus" title="Nicolaus Copernicus">Nicolaus Copernicus</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Heliocentrism" title="Heliocentrism">heliocentric theory</a>).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sub-Saharan_Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Africa" title="History of Africa">History of Africa</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Head_of_an_Oba_MET_DP231468.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="1697" decoding="async" height="259" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Head_of_an_Oba_MET_DP231468.jpg/220px-Head_of_an_Oba_MET_DP231468.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Head_of_an_Oba_MET_DP231468.jpg/330px-Head_of_an_Oba_MET_DP231468.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Head_of_an_Oba_MET_DP231468.jpg/440px-Head_of_an_Oba_MET_DP231468.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Head_of_an_Oba_MET_DP231468.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Brass" title="Brass">brass</a> "<a href="/wiki/Benin_Bronzes" title="Benin Bronzes">Benin Bronze</a>" from <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a></div></div></div>
<p>Medieval <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">sub-Saharan Africa</a> was home to many different civilizations. In the Horn of Africa, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aksum" title="Kingdom of Aksum">Kingdom of Aksum</a> declined in the 7th century. The <a href="/wiki/Zagwe_dynasty" title="Zagwe dynasty">Zagwe dynasty</a> that later emerged was famed for its rock cut architecture at <a href="/wiki/Lalibela" title="Lalibela">Lalibela</a>. The Zagwe would then fall to the <a href="/wiki/Solomonic_dynasty" title="Solomonic dynasty">Solomonic dynasty</a> who claimed descent from the Aksumite emperors<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[211]</a></sup> and would rule the country well into the 20th century. In the West African <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sahel</a> region, many Islamic empires rose, such as the <a href="/wiki/Mali_Empire" title="Mali Empire">Mali Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Songhai_Empire" title="Songhai Empire">Songhai Empire</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kanem%E2%80%93Bornu_Empire" title="Kanem–Bornu Empire">Kanem–Bornu Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015258,_379,_382,_393_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015258,_379,_382,_393-216">[212]</a></sup> They controlled the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Saharan_trade" title="Trans-Saharan trade">trans-Saharan trade</a> in gold, ivory, salt, and slaves.
</p><p>South of the Sahel, civilizations rose in the coastal forests. These include the <a href="/wiki/Yoruba_people" title="Yoruba people">Yoruba</a> city of <a href="/wiki/If%E1%BA%B9" title="Ifẹ">Ifẹ</a>, noted for its art,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[213]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Oyo_Empire" title="Oyo Empire">Oyo Empire</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Benin" title="Kingdom of Benin">Kingdom of Benin</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Edo_people" title="Edo people">Edo people</a> centered in <a href="/wiki/Benin_City" title="Benin City">Benin City</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Igbo_people" title="Igbo people">Igbo</a> <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Nri" title="Kingdom of Nri">Kingdom of Nri</a> which produced advanced bronze art at <a href="/wiki/Igbo-Ukwu" title="Igbo-Ukwu">Igbo-Ukwu</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Akan_people" title="Akan people">Akan</a> who are noted for their intricate architecture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[214]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[215]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">Central Africa</a> saw the formation of several states, including the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">Kingdom of Kongo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIliffe200782_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIliffe200782-220">[216]</a></sup> In what is now modern <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa" title="Southern Africa">Southern Africa</a>, native Africans created various kingdoms such as the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Mutapa" title="Kingdom of Mutapa">Kingdom of Mutapa</a>. They flourished through trade with the <a href="/wiki/Swahili_people" title="Swahili people">Swahili people</a> on the East African coast. They built large defensive stone structures without mortar such as <a href="/wiki/Great_Zimbabwe" title="Great Zimbabwe">Great Zimbabwe</a>, capital of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Zimbabwe" title="Kingdom of Zimbabwe">Kingdom of Zimbabwe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khami" title="Khami">Khami</a>, capital of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Butua" title="Kingdom of Butua">Kingdom of Butua</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEIliffe2007104–105_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIliffe2007104–105-221">[217]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Danangombe" title="Danangombe">Danangombe</a> (Dhlo-Dhlo), capital of the <a href="/wiki/Rozvi_Empire" title="Rozvi Empire">Rozvi Empire</a>. The Swahili people themselves were the inhabitants of the East African coast from Kenya to Mozambique who traded extensively with Asians and Arabs, who introduced them to Islam. They built many port cities such as <a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">Mombasa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">Zanzibar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kilwa_Kisiwani" title="Kilwa Kisiwani">Kilwa</a>, which were known to Chinese sailors under <a href="/wiki/Zheng_He" title="Zheng He">Zheng He</a> and Islamic geographers.
</p><p>Seafarers from Southeast Asia colonized <a href="/wiki/History_of_Madagascar" title="History of Madagascar">Madagascar</a> sometime between the 4th and 9th century,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDiamond199750_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDiamond199750-222">[218]</a></sup> creating what geographer <a href="/wiki/Jared_Diamond" title="Jared Diamond">Jared Diamond</a> called "the single most astonishing fact of human geography".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDiamond1997397_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDiamond1997397-223">[219]</a></sup> To reach Madagascar, the settlers crossed 6,000 miles of ocean in sailing canoes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015234_224-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015234-224">[220]</a></sup> probably without maps or compasses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDiamond1997397_223-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDiamond1997397-223">[219]</a></sup> A wave of <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu</a>-speaking migrants from southeastern Africa also arrived in Madagascar around 1000 CE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[221]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Asia">South Asia</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_India" title="History of India">History of India</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hoysala_emblem.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1760" data-file-width="1168" decoding="async" height="332" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Hoysala_emblem.JPG/220px-Hoysala_emblem.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Hoysala_emblem.JPG/330px-Hoysala_emblem.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Hoysala_emblem.JPG/440px-Hoysala_emblem.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hoysala_emblem.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Chennakeshava_Temple,_Belur" title="Chennakeshava Temple, Belur">Chennakesava Temple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belur,_Karnataka" title="Belur, Karnataka">Belur</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a></div></div></div>
<p>In northern <a href="/wiki/History_of_India" title="History of India">India</a>, after the fall (550 CE) of the <a href="/wiki/Gupta_Empire" title="Gupta Empire">Gupta Empire</a>, the region was divided into a complex and fluid network of smaller kingly states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[222]</a></sup>
</p><p>Early <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquests_in_the_Indian_subcontinent" title="Muslim conquests in the Indian subcontinent">Muslim incursions</a> began in the west in 712 CE, when the Arab <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">Umayyad Caliphate</a> annexed much of present-day <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>. Arab military advance was largely halted at that point, but Islam still spread in India, largely due to the influence of Arab merchants along the western coast.
</p><p>The ninth century saw a <a href="/wiki/Tripartite_Struggle" title="Tripartite Struggle">Tripartite Struggle</a> for control of northern India, among the <a href="/wiki/Gurjara-Pratihara_dynasty" title="Gurjara-Pratihara dynasty">Pratihara Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pala_Empire" title="Pala Empire">Pala Empire</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rashtrakuta_dynasty" title="Rashtrakuta dynasty">Rashtrakuta Empire</a>. Some of the important states that emerged in India during this time included the <a href="/wiki/Bahmani_Sultanate" title="Bahmani Sultanate">Bahmani Sultanate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vijayanagara_Empire" title="Vijayanagara Empire">Vijayanagara Empire</a>.
</p><p>Post-classical dynasties in South India included those of the <a href="/wiki/Chalukya_dynasty" title="Chalukya dynasty">Chalukyas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hoysala_Empire" title="Hoysala Empire">Hoysalas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chola_dynasty" title="Chola dynasty">Cholas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maratha_Empire" title="Maratha Empire">Marathas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Mysore" title="Kingdom of Mysore">Mysores</a>. Science, engineering, art, literature, astronomy, and philosophy flourished under the patronage of these kings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[223]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Northeast_Asia">Northeast Asia</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_East_Asia" title="History of East Asia">History of East Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Siberia" title="History of Siberia">History of Siberia</a></div>
<p>After a period of relative disunity, <a href="/wiki/History_of_China" title="History of China">China</a> was reunified by the <a href="/wiki/Sui_dynasty" title="Sui dynasty">Sui dynasty</a> in 589<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[224]</a></sup> and under the succeeding <a href="/wiki/Tang_dynasty" title="Tang dynasty">Tang dynasty</a> (618–907) China entered a <a href="/wiki/Golden_ages_of_China" title="Golden ages of China">Golden Age</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewis20091_229-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewis20091-229">[225]</a></sup> The Tang Empire competed with the <a href="/wiki/Tibetan_Empire" title="Tibetan Empire">Tibetan Empire</a> (618–842) for control of areas in Inner and Central Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhitfield2004193_230-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhitfield2004193-230">[226]</a></sup> The Tang dynasty eventually splintered, however, and after <a href="/wiki/Five_Dynasties_and_Ten_Kingdoms_period" title="Five Dynasties and Ten Kingdoms period">half a century of turmoil</a> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_Song_Dynasty" title="Northern Song Dynasty">Song dynasty</a> reunified much of China,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELorge20154–5_231-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELorge20154–5-231">[227]</a></sup> when it was, according to <a href="/wiki/William_H._McNeill_(historian)" title="William H. McNeill (historian)">William McNeill</a>, the "richest, most skilled, and most populous country on earth".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeill198250_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeill198250-232">[228]</a></sup> Pressure from nomadic empires to the north became increasingly urgent. By 1142, North China had been lost to the <a href="/wiki/Jurchen_people" title="Jurchen people">Jurchens</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Jin%E2%80%93Song_Wars" title="Jin–Song Wars">Jin–Song Wars</a>, and the Mongol Empire<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[229]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mongol_conquest_of_China" title="Mongol conquest of China">conquered all of China</a> in 1279, along with almost half of Eurasia's landmass. After about a century of Mongol <a href="/wiki/Yuan_dynasty" title="Yuan dynasty">Yuan dynasty</a> rule, the ethnic Chinese reasserted control with the founding of the <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a> in 1368.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="843" data-file-width="2520" decoding="async" height="100" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba.jpg/300px-M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba.jpg/450px-M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba.jpg/600px-M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:M%C5%8Dko_Sh%C5%ABrai_Ekotoba.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Battle during <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasions_of_Japan#Second_invasion_(1281)" title="Mongol invasions of Japan">1281 Mongol invasion of Japan</a></div></div></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/History_of_Japan" title="History of Japan">Japan</a>, the imperial lineage had been established by this time, and during the <a href="/wiki/Asuka_period" title="Asuka period">Asuka period</a> (538–710) the <a href="/wiki/Yamato_Province" title="Yamato Province">Yamato Province</a> developed into a clearly centralized state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HOJ_234-0"><a href="#cite_note-HOJ-234">[230]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> was introduced, and there was an emphasis on the adoption of elements of Chinese culture and <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Nara_period" title="Nara period">Nara period</a> of the 8th century was characterized by the appearance of a nascent <a href="/wiki/Japanese_literature" title="Japanese literature">literary culture</a>, as well as the development of Buddhist-inspired artwork and <a href="/wiki/Historic_Monuments_of_Ancient_Nara" title="Historic Monuments of Ancient Nara">architecture</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[231]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Courtiers_236-0"><a href="#cite_note-Courtiers-236">[232]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Heian_period" title="Heian period">Heian period</a> (794 to 1185) saw the peak of imperial power, followed by the rise of militarized clans, and the beginning of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feudal_Japan" title="Feudal Japan">Japanese feudalism</a>. The feudal period of Japanese history, dominated by powerful regional lords (<a href="/wiki/Daimyo" title="Daimyo">daimyos</a>) and the military rule of warlords (<a href="/wiki/Shogun" title="Shogun">shoguns</a>) such as the <a href="/wiki/Ashikaga_shogunate" title="Ashikaga shogunate">Ashikaga shogunate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tokugawa_shogunate" title="Tokugawa shogunate">Tokugawa shogunate</a>, stretched from 1185 to 1868. The emperor remained, but mostly as a figurehead, and the power of merchants was weak.
</p><p>Postclassical <a href="/wiki/History_of_Korea" title="History of Korea">Korea</a> saw the end of the <a href="/wiki/Three_Kingdoms_of_Korea" title="Three Kingdoms of Korea">Three Kingdoms</a> era, the three kingdoms being <a href="/wiki/Goguryeo" title="Goguryeo">Goguryeo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baekje" title="Baekje">Baekje</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Silla" title="Silla">Silla</a>. Silla conquered Baekje in 660, and Goguryeo in 668,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[233]</a></sup> marking the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Northern_and_Southern_States_period" title="Northern and Southern States period">Northern and Southern States period</a> (남북국시대), with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Later_Silla" title="Later Silla">Unified Silla</a> in the south and <a href="/wiki/Balhae" title="Balhae">Balhae</a>, a successor state to Goguryeo, in the north.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[234]</a></sup> In 892 CE, this arrangement reverted to the <a href="/wiki/Later_Three_Kingdoms" title="Later Three Kingdoms">Later Three Kingdoms</a>, with Goguryeo (then called <a href="/wiki/Taebong" title="Taebong">Taebong</a> and eventually named <a href="/wiki/Goryeo" title="Goryeo">Goryeo</a>) emerging as dominant, unifying the entire peninsula by 936.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kta_p113_239-0"><a href="#cite_note-kta_p113-239">[235]</a></sup> The founding Goryeo dynasty ruled until 1392, succeeded by the <a href="/wiki/Joseon" title="Joseon">Joseon</a> dynasty, which ruled for approximately 500 years.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Southeast_Asia">Southeast Asia</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Angkor_wat_temple.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="336" data-file-width="448" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Angkor_wat_temple.jpg/220px-Angkor_wat_temple.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Angkor_wat_temple.jpg/330px-Angkor_wat_temple.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Angkor_wat_temple.jpg/440px-Angkor_wat_temple.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Angkor_wat_temple.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Angkor_Wat" title="Angkor Wat">Angkor Wat</a> temple, <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a>, early 12th century</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Southeast_Asia" title="History of Southeast Asia">History of Southeast Asia</a></div>
<p>The beginning of the Middle Ages in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a> saw the fall (550 CE) of the <a href="/wiki/Funan" title="Funan">Kingdom of Funan</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Chenla" title="Chenla">Chenla Empire</a>, which was then replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Empire" title="Khmer Empire">Khmer Empire</a> (802 CE). The <a href="/wiki/Khmer_people" title="Khmer people">Khmer people</a>'s capital city, <a href="/wiki/Angkor" title="Angkor">Angkor</a>, was the largest city in the world prior to the industrial age<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans_et_al.200714279_240-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans_et_al.200714279-240">[236]</a></sup> and contained over a thousand temples, the most famous being <a href="/wiki/Angkor_Wat" title="Angkor Wat">Angkor Wat</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Sukhothai_Kingdom" title="Sukhothai Kingdom">Sukhothai</a> (1238 CE) and <a href="/wiki/Ayutthaya_Kingdom" title="Ayutthaya Kingdom">Ayutthaya</a> (1351 CE) kingdoms were major powers of the <a href="/wiki/Thai_people" title="Thai people">Thai people</a>, who were influenced by the Khmer.
</p><p>Starting in the 9th century, the <a href="/wiki/Pagan_Kingdom" title="Pagan Kingdom">Pagan Kingdom</a> rose to prominence in modern <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELieberman200391_241-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELieberman200391-241">[237]</a></sup> Its collapse brought about political fragmention that ended with the rise of the <a href="/wiki/First_Toungoo_Empire" title="First Toungoo Empire">Toungoo Empire</a> in the 16th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELieberman2003149–150_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELieberman2003149–150-242">[238]</a></sup> Other notable kingdoms of the period include the <a href="/wiki/Srivijaya" title="Srivijaya">Srivijayan Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lavo_Kingdom" title="Lavo Kingdom">Lavo Kingdom</a> (both coming into prominence in the 7th century), <a href="/wiki/Champa" title="Champa">Champa</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hariphunchai" title="Hariphunchai">Hariphunchai</a> (both about 750), <a href="/wiki/%C4%90%E1%BA%A1i_Vi%E1%BB%87t" title="Đại Việt">Đại Việt</a> (968), <a href="/wiki/Lan_Na" title="Lan Na">Lan Na</a> (13th century), <a href="/wiki/Majapahit" title="Majapahit">Majapahit</a> (1293), <a href="/wiki/Lan_Xang" title="Lan Xang">Lan Xang</a> (1354), and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ava" title="Kingdom of Ava">Ava Kingdom</a> (1364).
</p><p>This period saw the spread of Islam to present-day Indonesia (beginning in the 13th century) and the emergence of the <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_Malaysia" title="Peninsular Malaysia">Malay states</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Bruneian_Sultanate_(1368%E2%80%931888)" title="Bruneian Sultanate (1368–1888)">Brunei</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malacca_Sultanate" title="Malacca Sultanate">Malacca</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Philippines" title="History of the Philippines">Philippines</a>, several polities were formed such as <a href="/wiki/Tondo_(historical_polity)" title="Tondo (historical polity)">Tondo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cebu_(historical_state)" title="Cebu (historical state)">Cebu</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Butuan_(historical_polity)" title="Butuan (historical polity)">Butuan</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oceania">Oceania</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ahu_Tongariki,_15_moais.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2896" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Ahu_Tongariki%2C_15_moais.JPG/220px-Ahu_Tongariki%2C_15_moais.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Ahu_Tongariki%2C_15_moais.JPG/330px-Ahu_Tongariki%2C_15_moais.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Ahu_Tongariki%2C_15_moais.JPG/440px-Ahu_Tongariki%2C_15_moais.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ahu_Tongariki,_15_moais.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Moai" title="Moai">Moai</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapa_Nui" title="Rapa Nui">Rapa Nui</a> (Easter Island)</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Oceania" title="History of Oceania">History of Oceania</a></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Tu%CA%BBi_Tonga_Empire" title="Tuʻi Tonga Empire">Tuʻi Tonga Empire</a> was founded in the 10th century CE and expanded between 1200 and 1500. Tongan culture, language, and hegemony spread widely throughout eastern <a href="/wiki/Melanesia" title="Melanesia">Melanesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Micronesia" title="Micronesia">Micronesia</a>, and central <a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">Polynesia</a> during this period,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[239]</a></sup> influencing east 'Uvea, Rotuma, Futuna, Samoa, and Niue, as well as specific islands and parts of Micronesia (Kiribati, Pohnpei, and miscellaneous outliers), Vanuatu, and New Caledonia (specifically, the <a href="/wiki/Loyalty_Islands_Province" title="Loyalty Islands Province">Loyalty Islands</a>, with the main island being predominantly populated by the Melanesian <a href="/wiki/Kanak_people" title="Kanak people">Kanak people</a> and their cultures).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[240]</a></sup>
</p><p>In northern <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, there is evidence that some <a href="/wiki/Aboriginal_Australians" title="Aboriginal Australians">aboriginal groups</a> regularly <a href="/wiki/Makassan_contact_with_Australia" title="Makassan contact with Australia">traded with Makassarese fishermen</a> from Indonesia before the arrival of Europeans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[241]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[242]</a></sup>
</p><p>At around the same time, a powerful <a href="/wiki/Thalassocracy" title="Thalassocracy">thalassocracy</a> appeared in eastern Polynesia, centered around the <a href="/wiki/Society_Islands" title="Society Islands">Society Islands</a>, specifically on the sacred <a href="/wiki/Taputapuatea_marae" title="Taputapuatea marae">Taputapuatea marae</a>, which drew in eastern Polynesian colonists from places as far away as Hawaii, New Zealand (<i><a href="/wiki/Aotearoa" title="Aotearoa">Aotearoa</a></i>), and the Tuamotu Islands for political, spiritual, and economic reasons, until the unexplained collapse of regular long-distance voyaging in the eastern Pacific a few centuries before Europeans began exploring the area.
</p><p>Indigenous written records from this period are virtually nonexistent, as it seems that all Pacific Islanders, with the possible exception of the <a href="/wiki/Rapa_Nui_people" title="Rapa Nui people">Rapa Nui</a> and their currently undeciphered <a href="/wiki/Rongorongo" title="Rongorongo">Rongorongo</a> script, had no writing systems of any kind until after their introduction by European colonists. However, some indigenous prehistories can be estimated and academically reconstructed through careful, judicious analysis of native oral traditions, colonial ethnography, archaeology, physical anthropology, and linguistics research.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Americas">Americas</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Machu_Picchu,_Per%C3%BA,_2015-07-30,_DD_47.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5763" data-file-width="8669" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Machu_Picchu%2C_Per%C3%BA%2C_2015-07-30%2C_DD_47.JPG/220px-Machu_Picchu%2C_Per%C3%BA%2C_2015-07-30%2C_DD_47.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Machu_Picchu%2C_Per%C3%BA%2C_2015-07-30%2C_DD_47.JPG/330px-Machu_Picchu%2C_Per%C3%BA%2C_2015-07-30%2C_DD_47.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Machu_Picchu%2C_Per%C3%BA%2C_2015-07-30%2C_DD_47.JPG/440px-Machu_Picchu%2C_Per%C3%BA%2C_2015-07-30%2C_DD_47.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Machu_Picchu,_Per%C3%BA,_2015-07-30,_DD_47.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Machu_Picchu" title="Machu Picchu">Machu Picchu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inca_Empire" title="Inca Empire">Inca Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Americas" title="History of the Americas">History of the Americas</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_North_America" title="History of North America">History of North America</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Central_America" title="History of Central America">History of Central America</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Caribbean" title="History of the Caribbean">History of the Caribbean</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_South_America" title="History of South America">History of South America</a></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>, this period saw the rise of the <a href="/wiki/Mississippian_culture" title="Mississippian culture">Mississippian culture</a> in the modern-day <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> c. 800 CE, marked by the extensive 12th-century urban complex at <a href="/wiki/Cahokia" title="Cahokia">Cahokia</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Ancestral_Puebloans" title="Ancestral Puebloans">Ancestral Puebloans</a> and their predecessors (9th – 13th centuries) built extensive permanent settlements, including stone structures that would remain the largest buildings in North America until the 19th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFagan200535_247-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFagan200535-247">[243]</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">Mesoamerica</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Teotihuacan" title="Teotihuacan">Teotihuacan</a> civilization fell and the <a href="/wiki/Classic_Maya_collapse" title="Classic Maya collapse">classic Maya collapse</a> occurred.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015205,_208_248-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015205,_208-248">[244]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Aztec_Empire" title="Aztec Empire">Aztec Empire</a> came to dominate much of Mesoamerica in the 14th and 15th centuries.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>, the 15th century saw the rise of the Inca.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015397_177-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.2015397-177">[173]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Inca_Empire" title="Inca Empire">Inca Empire</a> or <i>Tawantinsuyu</i>, with its capital at <a href="/wiki/Cusco" title="Cusco">Cusco</a>, spanned the entire <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a>, making it the most extensive <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_era" title="Pre-Columbian era">pre-Columbian</a> civilization. The Inca were prosperous and advanced, known for an excellent <a href="/wiki/Inca_road_system" title="Inca road system">road system</a> and unrivaled <a href="/wiki/Masonry" title="Masonry">masonry</a>.
</p>
<h2><span id="Early_modern_period_.281450.E2.80.931750.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_modern_period_(1450–1750)">Early modern period (1450–1750)</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_period" title="Early modern period">Early modern period</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gutenburg_bible.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="442" data-file-width="337" decoding="async" height="289" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Gutenburg_bible.jpg/220px-Gutenburg_bible.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Gutenburg_bible.jpg/330px-Gutenburg_bible.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e3/Gutenburg_bible.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gutenburg_bible.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Gutenberg_Bible" title="Gutenberg Bible">Gutenberg Bible</a>, ca. 1450, produced using <a href="/wiki/Movable_type" title="Movable type">movable type</a></div></div></div><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:238px;max-width:238px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:132px;max-width:132px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Martin_Luther_by_Cranach-restoration.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="645" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="140"
