style="width:102px;max-width:102px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Luther_95_Thesen.png"><img alt="" data-file-height="4611" data-file-width="3228" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Luther_95_Thesen.png/100px-Luther_95_Thesen.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Luther_95_Thesen.png/150px-Luther_95_Thesen.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Luther_95_Thesen.png/200px-Luther_95_Thesen.png 2x" width="100"/></a></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a> initiated the <a href="/wiki/Reformation" title="Reformation">Reformation</a> in 1517 with his <i><a href="/wiki/Ninety-five_Theses" title="Ninety-five Theses">Ninety-five Theses</a></i></div></div></div></div>
<p>The "<a href="/wiki/Early_modern_period" title="Early modern period">early modern period</a>"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[e]</a></sup> was the period between the Middle Ages and the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>—roughly 1500 to 1800.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBentleyZiegler2008595_211-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBentleyZiegler2008595-211">[207]</a></sup> The early Modern period was characterized by the rise of science, and by increasingly rapid <a href="/wiki/History_of_technology" title="History of technology">technological progress</a>, <a href="/wiki/Secularization" title="Secularization">secularized</a> civic <a href="/wiki/Politics" title="Politics">politics</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Nation_state" title="Nation state">nation state</a>. <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">Capitalist economies</a> began their rise, initially in the <a href="/wiki/Maritime_republics" title="Maritime republics">northern Italian republics</a>. The early modern period saw the rise and dominance of <a href="/wiki/Mercantilism" title="Mercantilism">mercantilist</a> economic theory, and the decline and eventual disappearance, in much of the European sphere, of <a href="/wiki/Feudalism" title="Feudalism">feudalism</a>, serfdom, and the power of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>. The period included the <a href="/wiki/Reformation" title="Reformation">Reformation</a>, the disastrous <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a>, the Age of Discovery, European <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonial expansion</a>, the peak of European <a href="/wiki/Witch-hunt" title="Witch-hunt">witch-hunting</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Scientific_Revolution" title="Scientific Revolution">Scientific Revolution</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Age of Enlightenment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[f]</a></sup> During the early modern period, <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a> eventually became the majority faith throughout <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Europe" title="Northwestern Europe">Northwestern Europe</a> and in <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anglo-America" title="Anglo-America">English-speaking America</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clarke,_Beyer_251-0"><a href="#cite_note-Clarke,_Beyer-251">[245]</a></sup> and have developed <a href="/wiki/Protestant_culture" title="Protestant culture">their own culture</a>, with major contributions in education, the humanities and sciences, the political and social order, the economy and the arts and many other fields.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karl_Heussi_1956_pp._317–319_252-0"><a href="#cite_note-Karl_Heussi_1956_pp._317–319-252">[246]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Renaissance">Renaissance</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Da_Vinci_Vitruve_Luc_Viatour_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2966" data-file-width="2155" decoding="async" height="303" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Da_Vinci_Vitruve_Luc_Viatour_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Da_Vinci_Vitruve_Luc_Viatour_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Da_Vinci_Vitruve_Luc_Viatour_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Da_Vinci_Vitruve_Luc_Viatour_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Da_Vinci_Vitruve_Luc_Viatour_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Da_Vinci_Vitruve_Luc_Viatour_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Da_Vinci_Vitruve_Luc_Viatour_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">Leonardo da Vinci</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Vitruvian_Man" title="Vitruvian Man">Vitruvian Man</a></i> (c. 1490), <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a></div>
<p>Europe's Renaissance – the "rebirth" of classical culture, beginning in the 14th century and extending into the 16th – comprised the rediscovery of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classical_world" title="Classical world">classical world</a>'s cultural, scientific, and technological achievements, and the economic and social rise of Europe.
</p><p>The Renaissance engendered a culture of <a href="/wiki/Curiosity" title="Curiosity">inquisitiveness</a> which ultimately led to <a href="/wiki/Humanism" title="Humanism">Humanism</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis2012250–253_253-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHart-Davis2012250–253-253">[247]</a></sup> and the Scientific Revolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad2013683–685_254-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERobertsWestad2013683–685-254">[248]</a></sup>
</p><p>This period, which saw social and political upheavals, and revolutions in many <a href="/wiki/Intellectual" title="Intellectual">intellectual</a> pursuits, is also celebrated for its <a href="/wiki/Art" title="Art">artistic</a> developments and the attainments of such <a href="/wiki/Polymath" title="Polymath">polymaths</a> as <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">Leonardo da Vinci</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michelangelo" title="Michelangelo">Michelangelo</a>, who inspired the term "<a href="/wiki/Polymath" title="Polymath">Renaissance man</a>".
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_expansion">European expansion</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">Colonialism</a>, <a href="/wiki/16th_century" title="16th century">16th century</a>, and <a href="/wiki/17th_century" title="17th century">17th century</a></div>
<p>During this period, European powers came to dominate most of the world. Although the most developed regions of European classical civilization were more urbanized than any other region of the world, European civilization had undergone a lengthy period of gradual decline and collapse. During the early modern period, Europe was able to regain its dominance; historians still debate the causes.
</p><p>This era was characterized by the rise of maritime European empires in the 15th, 16th, and 17th centuries, first the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empires</a>, and later the <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_overseas_possessions" title="English overseas possessions">English</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">Dutch Empires</a>. In the 17th century, globalization became also a private business phenomenon when <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chartered_companies" title="Chartered companies">chartered companies</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">English East India Company</a> (founded in 1600), often described as the first <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational corporation</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a> (founded in 1602) were established.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:OrteliusWorldMap.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3942" data-file-width="5788" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/OrteliusWorldMap.jpeg/220px-OrteliusWorldMap.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/OrteliusWorldMap.jpeg/330px-OrteliusWorldMap.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/OrteliusWorldMap.jpeg/440px-OrteliusWorldMap.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:OrteliusWorldMap.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Abraham_Ortelius#Map_publisher" title="Abraham Ortelius">1570 world map</a>, showing Europeans' discoveries</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a> brought a broad change in globalization, being the first period in which Eurasia and Africa engaged in substantial cultural, material and biologic exchange with the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>. It began in the late 15th century, when the two kingdoms of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> – <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Portugal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Castile" title="Kingdom of Castile">Castile</a> – sent the first exploratory voyages around the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a> and to the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>, "discovered" in 1492 by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a>. Shortly before the turn of the 16th century, Portuguese started establishing <a href="/wiki/Factory_(trading_post)" title="Factory (trading post)">factories</a> from Africa to Asia and Brazil, to deal with the trade of local products like <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slaves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spice" title="Spice">spices</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lumber" title="Lumber">lumber</a>, introducing an international business center under a royal monopoly, the <a href="/wiki/Casa_da_%C3%8Dndia" title="Casa da Índia">House of India</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[249]</a></sup>
</p><p>Global integration continued with the <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">European colonization of the Americas</a> initiating the <a href="/wiki/Columbian_exchange" title="Columbian exchange">Columbian exchange</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[250]</a></sup> the enormous widespread exchange of plants, animals, foods, human populations (including slaves), <a href="/wiki/Infection" title="Infection">communicable diseases</a>, and culture between the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Hemisphere" title="Eastern Hemisphere">Eastern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemispheres</a>. It was one of the most significant global events concerning <a href="/wiki/Ecology" title="Ecology">ecology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">culture</a> in history. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Columbian_Exchange" title="Columbian Exchange">New crops</a> that had come from the Americas via the European seafarers in the 16th century significantly contributed to the world's population growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[251]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_developments">Regional developments</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Greater_Middle_East_2">Greater Middle East</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hagia_Sophia_(Holy_Wisdom)_-_the_epitome_of_Byzantine_architecture_-_panoramio.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1130" data-file-width="1700" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Hagia_Sophia_%28Holy_Wisdom%29_-_the_epitome_of_Byzantine_architecture_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Hagia_Sophia_%28Holy_Wisdom%29_-_the_epitome_of_Byzantine_architecture_-_panoramio.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Hagia_Sophia_%28Holy_Wisdom%29_-_the_epitome_of_Byzantine_architecture_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-Hagia_Sophia_%28Holy_Wisdom%29_-_the_epitome_of_Byzantine_architecture_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Hagia_Sophia_%28Holy_Wisdom%29_-_the_epitome_of_Byzantine_architecture_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-Hagia_Sophia_%28Holy_Wisdom%29_-_the_epitome_of_Byzantine_architecture_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hagia_Sophia_(Holy_Wisdom)_-_the_epitome_of_Byzantine_architecture_-_panoramio.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hagia_Sophia" title="Hagia Sophia">Hagia Sophia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a>), <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Ottoman Empire, after <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople" title="Fall of Constantinople">conquering Constantinople</a> in 1453, quickly came to dominate the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBentleySubrahmanyamWiesner-Hanks2015a417_258-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBentleySubrahmanyamWiesner-Hanks2015a417-258">[252]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Persia</a> came under the rule of the <a href="/wiki/Safavid_dynasty" title="Safavid dynasty">Safavid Empire</a> in 1501, succeeded by the <a href="/wiki/Afsharid_dynasty" title="Afsharid dynasty">Afsharid Empire</a> in 1736, the <a href="/wiki/Zand_dynasty" title="Zand dynasty">Zand Empire</a> in 1751, and the <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">Qajar Empire</a> in 1794. In <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Wattasid_dynasty" title="Wattasid dynasty">Wattasid Sultanate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zayyanid_dynasty" title="Zayyanid dynasty">Zayyanid Sultanate</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hafsid_dynasty" title="Hafsid dynasty">Hafsid Sultanate</a> remained as independent <a href="/wiki/Berbers" title="Berbers">Berber</a> states until the 16th century. Areas to the north and east in <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a> were held by the <a href="/wiki/Uzbeks" title="Uzbeks">Uzbeks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pashtuns" title="Pashtuns">Pashtuns</a>. At the start of the 19th century, the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> began its <a href="/wiki/Russian_conquest_of_the_Caucasus" title="Russian conquest of the Caucasus">conquest</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe_2">Europe</span></h4>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/History_of_Russia" title="History of Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivan_the_Terrible" title="Ivan the Terrible">Ivan the Terrible</a> was crowned in 1547 as the first <a href="/wiki/Tsar" title="Tsar">Tsar</a> of Russia, and by annexing the Turkic khanates in the east, transformed Russia into a regional power. The countries of Western Europe, while expanding prodigiously through technological advancement and colonial conquest, competed with each other economically and militarily in a state of almost constant <a href="/wiki/List_of_wars:_1500%E2%80%931799" title="List of wars: 1500–1799">war</a>. Often the wars had a <a href="/wiki/European_wars_of_religion" title="European wars of religion">religious dimension</a>, either Catholic versus Protestant, or (primarily in Eastern Europe) Christian versus Muslim. Wars of particular note include the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolutionary_Wars" title="French Revolutionary Wars">French Revolutionary Wars</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBentleySubrahmanyamWiesner-Hanks2015b41,_44,_47,_343_259-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBentleySubrahmanyamWiesner-Hanks2015b41,_44,_47,_343-259">[253]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a> <a href="/wiki/Coup_of_18_Brumaire" title="Coup of 18 Brumaire">came to power</a> in France in 1799, an event foreshadowing the Napoleonic Wars of the early 19th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a529_260-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a529-260">[254]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sub-Saharan_Africa_2">Sub-Saharan Africa</span></h4>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/History_of_Africa" title="History of Africa">Africa</a>, this period saw a decline in many civilizations and an advancement in others. The <a href="/wiki/Swahili_coast" title="Swahili coast">Swahili coast</a> declined after coming under the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a> and later the <a href="/wiki/Omani_Empire" title="Omani Empire">Omani Empire</a>. In <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Songhai_Empire" title="Songhai Empire">Songhai Empire</a> fell to the Moroccans in 1591 when they <a href="/wiki/Saadian_invasion_of_the_Songhai_Empire" title="Saadian invasion of the Songhai Empire">invaded with firearms</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Bono_state" title="Bono state">Bono state</a> gave birth to numerous <a href="/wiki/Akan_people" title="Akan people">Akan</a> states in its wake in search of gold such as <a href="/wiki/Akwamu" title="Akwamu">Akwamu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Akyem" title="Akyem">Akyem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fante_people" title="Fante people">Fante</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adansi" title="Adansi">Adansi</a> etc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[255]</a></sup> The South African <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Zimbabwe" title="Kingdom of Zimbabwe">Kingdom of Zimbabwe</a> gave way to smaller kingdoms such as <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Mutapa" title="Kingdom of Mutapa">Mutapa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Butua" title="Kingdom of Butua">Butua</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rozvi_Empire" title="Rozvi Empire">Rozvi</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Empire" title="Ethiopian Empire">Ethiopian Empire</a> suffered from the 1531 invasion by the neighboring Muslim <a href="/wiki/Adal_Sultanate" title="Adal Sultanate">Adal Sultanate</a>, and in 1769 entered the <a href="/wiki/Zemene_Mesafint" title="Zemene Mesafint">Zemene Mesafint</a> (Age of Princes) during which the Emperor became a figurehead and the country was ruled by warlords, though the royal line later would recover under Emperor <a href="/wiki/Tewodros_II" title="Tewodros II">Tewodros II</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Ajuran_Sultanate" title="Ajuran Sultanate">Ajuran Sultanate</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">Horn of Africa</a>, began to decline in the 17th century, succeeded by the <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_the_Geledi" title="Sultanate of the Geledi">Geledi Sultanate</a>. Other civilizations in Africa advanced during this period. The <a href="/wiki/Oyo_Empire" title="Oyo Empire">Oyo Empire</a> experienced its golden age, as did the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Benin" title="Kingdom of Benin">Kingdom of Benin</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Ashanti_Empire" title="Ashanti Empire">Ashanti Empire</a> rose to power in what is modern day <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a> in 1670. The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kongo" title="Kingdom of Kongo">Kingdom of Kongo</a> also thrived during this period.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Asia_2">South Asia</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Taj_Mahal_in_March_2004.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1681" data-file-width="2040" decoding="async" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Taj_Mahal_in_March_2004.jpg/220px-Taj_Mahal_in_March_2004.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Taj_Mahal_in_March_2004.jpg/330px-Taj_Mahal_in_March_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Taj_Mahal_in_March_2004.jpg/440px-Taj_Mahal_in_March_2004.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Taj_Mahal_in_March_2004.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Taj_Mahal" title="Taj Mahal">Taj Mahal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a></div></div></div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughal Empire</a> began in 1526 and lasted for two centuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein2010159_262-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein2010159-262">[256]</a></sup> Starting in the northwest, the Mughal Empire would by the late 17th century come to rule the entire subcontinent,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[257]</a></sup> except for the southernmost Indian provinces, which would remain independent. Against the Muslim Mughal Empire, the Hindu <a href="/wiki/Maratha_Empire" title="Maratha Empire">Maratha Empire</a> was founded on the west coast in 1674, gradually gaining territory—a majority of present-day India—from the Mughals over several decades, particularly in the <a href="/wiki/Mughal%E2%80%93Maratha_Wars" title="Mughal–Maratha Wars">Mughal–Maratha Wars</a> (1681–1701). The Maratha Empire would in 1818 fall under the control of the <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">British East India Company</a>, with all former Maratha and Mughal authority devolving in 1858 to the <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British Raj</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Northeast_Asia_2">Northeast Asia</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chemin_de_ronde_muraille_long.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Chemin_de_ronde_muraille_long.JPG/220px-Chemin_de_ronde_muraille_long.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Chemin_de_ronde_muraille_long.JPG/330px-Chemin_de_ronde_muraille_long.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Chemin_de_ronde_muraille_long.JPG/440px-Chemin_de_ronde_muraille_long.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chemin_de_ronde_muraille_long.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming dynasty</a> section, <a href="/wiki/Great_Wall_of_China" title="Great Wall of China">Great Wall of China</a></div></div></div>
<p>In China, the <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">Ming</a> gave way in 1644 to the <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">Qing</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBentleySubrahmanyamWiesner-Hanks2015a116_264-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBentleySubrahmanyamWiesner-Hanks2015a116-264">[258]</a></sup> the last Chinese imperial dynasty, which would rule until 1912.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillMcNeill2003247_265-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillMcNeill2003247-265">[259]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/History_of_Japan" title="History of Japan">Japan</a> experienced its <a href="/wiki/Azuchi%E2%80%93Momoyama_period" title="Azuchi–Momoyama period">Azuchi–Momoyama period</a> (1568–1603), followed by the <a href="/wiki/Edo_period" title="Edo period">Edo period</a> (1603–1868). The <a href="/wiki/History_of_Korea" title="History of Korea">Korean</a> <a href="/wiki/Joseon" title="Joseon">Joseon dynasty</a> (1392–1910) ruled throughout this period, successfully repelling 16th and 17th century invasions from Japan and China. Expanded maritime trade with Europe significantly affected China and Japan during this period, particularly by the Portuguese who had a presence in <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nagasaki" title="Nagasaki">Nagasaki</a>. However, China and Japan would later pursue <a href="/wiki/Isolationism" title="Isolationism">isolationist</a> policies designed to eliminate foreign influences.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Southeast_Asia_2">Southeast Asia</span></h4>
<p>In 1511, the Portuguese overthrew the <a href="/wiki/Malacca_Sultanate" title="Malacca Sultanate">Malacca Sultanate</a> in present-day Malaysia and Indonesian <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a>. The Portuguese held this important trading territory (and the valuable associated navigational strait) until overthrown by the Dutch in 1641. The <a href="/wiki/Johor_Sultanate" title="Johor Sultanate">Johor Sultanate</a>, centred on the southern tip of the Malay Peninsula, became the dominant trading power in the region. <a href="/wiki/European_colonisation_of_Southeast_Asia" title="European colonisation of Southeast Asia">European colonization</a> expanded with the Dutch in <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Indonesia</a>, the Portuguese in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Timor" title="Portuguese Timor">East Timor</a>, and the Spanish in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">Philippines</a>. Into the 19th century, European expansion would affect the whole of Southeast Asia, with the British in <a href="/wiki/British_rule_in_Burma" title="British rule in Burma">Myanmar</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Malaya" title="British Malaya">Malaysia</a>, and the French in <a href="/wiki/French_Indochina" title="French Indochina">Indochina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a336_266-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a336-266">[260]</a></sup> Only <a href="/wiki/History_of_Thailand" title="History of Thailand">Thailand</a> would successfully resist colonization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a336_266-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a336-266">[260]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Oceania_2">Oceania</span></h4>
<p>The Pacific islands of <a href="/wiki/History_of_Oceania" title="History of Oceania">Oceania</a> would also be affected by European contact, starting with the circumnavigational voyage of <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">Ferdinand Magellan</a>, who landed on the <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Islands" title="Mariana Islands">Marianas</a> and other islands in 1521. Also notable were the voyages (1642–1644) of <a href="/wiki/Abel_Tasman" title="Abel Tasman">Abel Tasman</a> to present-day <a href="/wiki/History_of_Australia" title="History of Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_New_Zealand" title="History of New Zealand">New Zealand</a> and nearby islands, and the voyages (1768–1779) of Captain <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a>, who made the first recorded European contact with <a href="/wiki/History_of_Hawaii" title="History of Hawaii">Hawaii</a>. Britain would found its <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_New_South_Wales" title="Colony of New South Wales">first colony</a> on Australia in 1788.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMatsuda2012161_267-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMatsuda2012161-267">[261]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Americas_2">Americas</span></h4>
<p>In the Americas, several <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">European powers</a> vigorously colonized the newly discovered continents, largely displacing the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">indigenous populations</a>, and destroying the advanced civilizations of the <a href="/wiki/Aztec_Empire" title="Aztec Empire">Aztecs</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Inca_Empire" title="Inca Empire">Incas</a>. Spain, Portugal, Britain, and France all made extensive territorial claims, and undertook large-scale settlement, including the importation of large numbers of African <a href="/wiki/History_of_slavery#Americas" title="History of slavery">slaves</a>. Portugal claimed <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Brazil" title="Colonial Brazil">Brazil</a>. Spain claimed the rest of <a href="/wiki/History_of_South_America" title="History of South America">South America</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">Mesoamerica</a>, and southern <a href="/wiki/History_of_North_America" title="History of North America">North America</a>. Britain colonized the east coast of North America, and France colonized the central region of North America. Russia made incursions onto the northwest coast of North America, with a first colony in present-day <a href="/wiki/History_of_Alaska" title="History of Alaska">Alaska</a> in 1784, and the outpost of <a href="/wiki/Fort_Ross,_California" title="Fort Ross, California">Fort Ross</a> in present-day <a href="/wiki/History_of_California" title="History of California">California</a> in 1812.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[262]</a></sup> In 1762, in the midst of the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a>, France secretly ceded most of its North American claims to Spain in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Fontainebleau_(1762)" title="Treaty of Fontainebleau (1762)">Treaty of Fontainebleau</a>. Thirteen of the British colonies declared independence as the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_States" title="History of the United States">United States of America</a> in 1776, ratified by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">Treaty of Paris</a> in 1783, ending the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETindall_&amp;_Shi_2010219,_254_269-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETindall_&amp;_Shi_2010219,_254-269">[263]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon Bonaparte</a> won France's claims back from Spain in the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a> in 1800, but sold them to the United States in 1803 as the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase" title="Louisiana Purchase">Louisiana Purchase</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETindall_&amp;_Shi_2010352_270-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETindall_&amp;_Shi_2010352-270">[264]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Late_modern_period_.281750.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Late_modern_period_(1750–present)">Late modern period (1750–present)</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Late_modern_period" title="Late modern period">Late modern period</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="18th_and_19th_centuries">18th and 19th centuries</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/18th_century" title="18th century">18th century</a>, <a href="/wiki/19th_century" title="19th century">19th century</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Long_nineteenth_century" title="Long nineteenth century">Long nineteenth century</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Age_of_Imperialism" title="Age of Imperialism">Age of Imperialism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Revolution" title="Age of Revolution">Age of Revolution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_Revolution" title="Diplomatic Revolution">Diplomatic Revolution</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="760" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg/220px-Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg/330px-Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg/440px-Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maquina_vapor_Watt_ETSIIM.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/James_Watt" title="James Watt">James Watt</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Steam_engine" title="Steam engine">steam engine</a> powered the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The Scientific Revolution changed humanity's understanding of the world and was followed by the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, a major transformation of the world's economies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b189_271-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b189-271">[265]</a></sup> The Scientific Revolution in the 17th century had had little immediate effect on industrial technology;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b189_271-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b189-271">[265]</a></sup> only in the second half of the 19th century did scientific advances begin to be applied substantially to practical <a href="/wiki/Invention" title="Invention">invention</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b190–91_272-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b190–91-272">[266]</a></sup> The Industrial Revolution began in <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">Great Britain</a> and used new modes of production—the <a href="/wiki/Factory" title="Factory">factory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mass_production" title="Mass production">mass production</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mechanization" title="Mechanization">mechanization</a>—to manufacture a wide array of goods faster and using less labour than previously required.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a137_273-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a137-273">[267]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Age of Enlightenment</a> also led to the beginnings of modern <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a> in the late-18th century American and <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French</a> revolutions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b189_271-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b189-271">[265]</a></sup> Democracy and <a href="/wiki/Republicanism" title="Republicanism">republicanism</a> would grow to have a profound effect on world events and on <a href="/wiki/Quality_of_life" title="Quality of life">quality of life</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:World_1898_empires_colonies_territory.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="624" data-file-width="1560" decoding="async" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/World_1898_empires_colonies_territory.png/400px-World_1898_empires_colonies_territory.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/World_1898_empires_colonies_territory.png/600px-World_1898_empires_colonies_territory.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/World_1898_empires_colonies_territory.png/800px-World_1898_empires_colonies_territory.png 2x" width="400"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:World_1898_empires_colonies_territory.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Empire" title="Empire">Empires</a> of the world in 1898</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wright_First_Flight_1903Dec17_(full_restore_115).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5178" data-file-width="7162" decoding="async" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Wright_First_Flight_1903Dec17_%28full_restore_115%29.jpg/220px-Wright_First_Flight_1903Dec17_%28full_restore_115%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Wright_First_Flight_1903Dec17_%28full_restore_115%29.jpg/330px-Wright_First_Flight_1903Dec17_%28full_restore_115%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Wright_First_Flight_1903Dec17_%28full_restore_115%29.jpg/440px-Wright_First_Flight_1903Dec17_%28full_restore_115%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wright_First_Flight_1903Dec17_(full_restore_115).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The first aeroplane, the <i><a href="/wiki/Wright_Flyer" title="Wright Flyer">Wright Flyer</a></i>, flew on 17 December 1903.</div></div></div>
<p>After Europeans had achieved influence and control over the Americas, <a href="/wiki/Imperialism" title="Imperialism">imperial</a> activities turned to the lands of Asia and Oceania. Britain gained control of the Indian subcontinent, Burma and the <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_Malaysia" title="Peninsular Malaysia">Malay Peninsula</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Cochinchina_campaign" title="Cochinchina campaign">French took Indochina</a>; while the Dutch cemented their control over the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a336_266-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a336-266">[260]</a></sup> China was devastated by the <a href="/wiki/Taiping_Rebellion" title="Taiping Rebellion">Taiping Rebellion</a>, history's bloodiest civil war, which killed 20–30 million people between 1850 and 1864.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274">[268]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPomeranzMcNeill2015623_275-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPomeranzMcNeill2015623-275">[269]</a></sup> The British also colonized Australia, New Zealand and South Africa with large numbers of British colonists emigrating to these colonies. Russia colonized large pre-agricultural areas of Siberia. In the late-19th century, the European powers <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">divided the remaining areas of Africa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a562_276-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a562-276">[270]</a></sup> Within Europe, economic and military challenges created a system of <a href="/wiki/Nation_state" title="Nation state">nation states</a>, and ethno-cultural groupings began to identify themselves as distinctive nations with aspirations for cultural and political autonomy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a306,_310–11_277-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a306,_310–11-277">[271]</a></sup> This <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">nationalism</a> would become important to peoples across the world in the 20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a312_278-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a312-278">[272]</a></sup>
</p><p>The advantages that Europe had developed by the mid-18th century were two: an <a href="/wiki/Entrepreneurship" title="Entrepreneurship">entrepreneurial</a> culture,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279"><a href="#cite_note-279">[273]</a></sup> and the wealth generated by the Atlantic trade (including the <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Africa" title="Slavery in Africa">African slave trade</a>). The profits of the slave trade and of <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indian</a> plantations amounted to 5% of the <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Economic history of the United Kingdom">British economy</a> at the time of the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280">[274]</a></sup> Some historians conclude that, in 1750, <a href="/wiki/Workforce_productivity" title="Workforce productivity">labour productivity</a> in the most developed regions of China was still on a par with that of Europe's Atlantic economy;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281"><a href="#cite_note-281">[275]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPomeranz200031–32_282-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPomeranz200031–32-282">[276]</a></sup> other historians such as <a href="/wiki/Angus_Maddison" title="Angus Maddison">Angus Maddison</a> hold that the per-capita productivity of western Europe had by the late <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> surpassed that of all other regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-283"><a href="#cite_note-283">[277]</a></sup>
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Second_Industrial_Revolution" title="Second Industrial Revolution">Second Industrial Revolution</a>, a new set of technological advances including electrical power, the <a href="/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine" title="Internal combustion engine">internal combustion engine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Assembly_line" title="Assembly line">assembly line</a> manufacturing increased productivity once again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELandes1969235_284-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELandes1969235-284">[278]</a></sup> Meanwhile, industrial <a href="/wiki/Pollution" title="Pollution">pollution</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_environment" title="Natural environment">environmental</a> damage, present since the discovery of fire and the beginning of civilization, accelerated drastically.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a80_285-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a80-285">[279]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/20th_century" title="20th century">20th century</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_history" title="Contemporary history">Contemporary history</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">Interwar period</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roaring_Twenties" title="Roaring Twenties">Roaring Twenties</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green_Revolution" title="Green Revolution">Green Revolution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">Space exploration</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Digital_Revolution" title="Digital Revolution">Digital Revolution</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Irish_Rifles_ration_party_Somme_July_1916.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="671" data-file-width="949" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Royal_Irish_Rifles_ration_party_Somme_July_1916.jpg/220px-Royal_Irish_Rifles_ration_party_Somme_July_1916.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Royal_Irish_Rifles_ration_party_Somme_July_1916.jpg/330px-Royal_Irish_Rifles_ration_party_Somme_July_1916.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Royal_Irish_Rifles_ration_party_Somme_July_1916.jpg/440px-Royal_Irish_Rifles_ration_party_Somme_July_1916.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Irish_Rifles_ration_party_Somme_July_1916.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> <a href="/wiki/Trench_warfare" title="Trench warfare">trench warfare</a></div></div></div>
<p>The 20th century opened with Europe at an apex of wealth and power, and with much of the world under its direct <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonial</a> control or its indirect domination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a313–14_286-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a313–14-286">[280]</a></sup> Much of the rest of the world was influenced by heavily Europeanized nations: the United States and Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a313–14_286-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a313–14-286">[280]</a></sup> As the century unfolded, however, the global system dominated by rival powers was subjected to severe strains, and ultimately yielded to a more fluid structure of independent nation states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a306_287-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a306-287">[281]</a></sup>
</p><p>This transformation was catalyzed by wars of unparalleled scope and devastation. <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> led to the collapse of four empires – <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a>, the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> – and weakened the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Armenian_genocide" title="Armenian genocide">Armenian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sayfo" title="Sayfo">Assyrian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Greek_genocide" title="Greek genocide">Greek genocides</a> were the systematic destruction, mass murder, and expulsion during World War I of the <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Assyrian_people" title="Assyrian people">Assyrians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a> in the Ottoman Empire, spearheaded by the ruling <a href="/wiki/Committee_of_Union_and_Progress" title="Committee of Union and Progress">Committee of Union and Progress</a> (CUP).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESuny2015245,_330_288-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESuny2015245,_330-288">[282]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBozarslan_''et_al.''2015187_289-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBozarslan_''et_al.''2015187-289">[283]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the war's aftermath, powerful ideologies rose to prominence. The <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">Russian Revolution</a> of 1917 created the first <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">communist</a> state,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a450_290-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a450-290">[284]</a></sup> while the 1920s and 1930s saw <a href="/wiki/Militarism" title="Militarism">militaristic</a> <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">fascist</a> dictatorships gain control in <a href="/wiki/Fascist_Italy_(1922%E2%80%931943)" title="Fascist Italy (1922–1943)">Italy</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a452_291-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a452-291">[285]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Germany</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a452_291-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a452-291">[285]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Francoist_Spain" title="Francoist Spain">Spain</a>, and elsewhere. From 1918 to 1920, the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_flu" title="Spanish flu">Spanish flu</a> caused the deaths of at least 25 million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a246–7_292-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a246–7-292">[286]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nagasakibomb.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3877" data-file-width="3245" decoding="async" height="263" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Nagasakibomb.jpg/220px-Nagasakibomb.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Nagasakibomb.jpg/330px-Nagasakibomb.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Nagasakibomb.jpg/440px-Nagasakibomb.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nagasakibomb.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atomic_bombings" title="Atomic bombings">Atomic bombings</a>: <a href="/wiki/Hiroshima" title="Hiroshima">Hiroshima</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nagasaki" title="Nagasaki">Nagasaki</a>, 1945</div></div></div>
<p>Ongoing national rivalries, exacerbated by the economic turmoil of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, helped precipitate World War II. The <a href="/wiki/Militarism" title="Militarism">militaristic</a> <a href="/wiki/Dictatorship" title="Dictatorship">dictatorships</a> of Europe and Japan pursued an ultimately doomed course of <a href="/wiki/Imperialism" title="Imperialism">imperialist</a> <a href="/wiki/Expansionism" title="Expansionism">expansionism</a>, in the course of which Nazi Germany, under <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>, orchestrated the <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a> of six million Jews in <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">the Holocaust</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a423–4_293-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a423–4-293">[287]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Imperial Japan</a> <a href="/wiki/Japanese_war_crimes" title="Japanese war crimes">murdered</a> millions of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people" title="Chinese people">Chinese</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a507–8_294-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a507–8-294">[288]</a></sup>
</p><p>The World War II defeat of the <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis powers</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied powers</a> opened the way for the advance of communism into Eastern Europe, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Vietnam" title="North Vietnam">North Vietnam</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a319,_451_295-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a319,_451-295">[289]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:My_Lai_massacre_woman_and_children.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="975" data-file-width="650" decoding="async" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/My_Lai_massacre_woman_and_children.jpg/220px-My_Lai_massacre_woman_and_children.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/My_Lai_massacre_woman_and_children.jpg/330px-My_Lai_massacre_woman_and_children.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/My_Lai_massacre_woman_and_children.jpg/440px-My_Lai_massacre_woman_and_children.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:My_Lai_massacre_woman_and_children.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Civilians (here, <a href="/wiki/M%E1%BB%B9_Lai_massacre" title="Mỹ Lai massacre">Mỹ Lai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>, 1968) suffered greatly in 20th-century wars.</div></div></div>
<p>When World War II ended in 1945, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> was founded in the hope of preventing future wars,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fasulo1_296-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fasulo1-296">[290]</a></sup> as the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> had been formed following World War I.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a324_297-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a324-297">[291]</a></sup> World War II had left two countries, the United States and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, with principal power to influence <a href="/wiki/International_relations" title="International relations">international affairs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy1987357_298-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy1987357-298">[292]</a></sup> Each was suspicious of the other and feared a global spread of the other's, respectively capitalist and communist, political-economic model. This led to the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, a 45-year stand-off and <a href="/wiki/Arms_race" title="Arms race">arms race</a> between the United States and its allies, on one hand, and the Soviet Union and its allies on the other.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllison2018126_299-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllison2018126-299">[293]</a></sup>
</p><p>With the development of <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">nuclear weapons</a> during World War II, and with their subsequent <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_proliferation" title="Nuclear proliferation">proliferation</a>, all of humanity were put at risk of <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_warfare" title="Nuclear warfare">nuclear war</a> between the two superpowers, as demonstrated by <a href="/wiki/List_of_nuclear_close_calls" title="List of nuclear close calls">many incidents</a>, most prominently the October 1962 <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis" title="Cuban Missile Crisis">Cuban Missile Crisis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b321,_330_300-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b321,_330-300">[294]</a></sup> Such war <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_holocaust" title="Nuclear holocaust">being viewed as impractical</a>, the superpowers instead waged <a href="/wiki/Proxy_war" title="Proxy war">proxy wars</a> in non-nuclear-armed <a href="/wiki/Third_World" title="Third World">Third World</a> countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllison2018127–128_301-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllison2018127–128-301">[295]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStevenson2020_302-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStevenson2020-302">[296]</a></sup> Between 1969 and 1972, as part of the Cold War <a href="/wiki/Space_Race" title="Space Race">Space Race</a>, twelve American <a href="/wiki/Astronaut" title="Astronaut">astronauts</a> <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">landed</a> on the Moon and safely returned to Earth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGleick2019_303-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGleick2019-303">[297]</a></sup>
</p><p>In China, <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a> implemented <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Industrialization" title="Industrialization">industrialization</a> and <a href="/wiki/Collective_farming" title="Collective farming">collectivization</a> reforms as part of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Leap_Forward" title="Great Leap Forward">Great Leap Forward</a> (1958–1962), leading to the <a href="/wiki/Great_Chinese_Famine" title="Great Chinese Famine">starvation deaths</a> (1959–1961) of 30–40 million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a459–60_304-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a459–60-304">[298]</a></sup> After Mao's death, China entered a period of economic liberalization and rapid growth, with the economy expanding by 6.6% per year from 1978 to 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPomeranzMcNeill2015629_305-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPomeranzMcNeill2015629-305">[299]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Cold War ended peacefully in 1991 after the <a href="/wiki/Pan-European_Picnic" title="Pan-European Picnic">Pan-European Picnic</a>, the subsequent fall of the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Curtain" title="Iron Curtain">Iron Curtain</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall" title="Berlin Wall">Berlin Wall</a>, and the collapse of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">Soviet Union collapsed</a>, partly due to its inability to compete economically with the United States and Western Europe. The United States likewise began to show signs of slippage in its geopolitical influence,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcCormick1995155_306-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcCormick1995155-306">[300]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllison2018129–131_307-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllison2018129–131-307">[301]</a></sup> and its <a href="/wiki/Economic_inequality" title="Economic inequality">economic inequality</a> increased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrowning201816_308-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrowning201816-308">[302]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStiglitz2018_309-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStiglitz2018-309">[303]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the early postwar decades, the colonies in Asia and Africa of the Belgian, British, Dutch, French, and other west European empires won their formal independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbernethy2000133_310-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbernethy2000133-310">[304]</a></sup> Most Western European and Central European countries gradually formed a political and economic community, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, which expanded eastward to include former <a href="/wiki/Satellite_state#Post-World_War_II" title="Satellite state">Soviet satellite states</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDinan2004xiii,_8–9_311-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDinan2004xiii,_8–9-311">[305]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_17_Cernan_on_moon.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4029" data-file-width="3904" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Apollo_17_Cernan_on_moon.jpg/220px-Apollo_17_Cernan_on_moon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Apollo_17_Cernan_on_moon.jpg/330px-Apollo_17_Cernan_on_moon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Apollo_17_Cernan_on_moon.jpg/440px-Apollo_17_Cernan_on_moon.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apollo_17_Cernan_on_moon.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Last Moon landing: <a href="/wiki/Apollo_17" title="Apollo 17">Apollo 17</a> (1972)</div></div></div>
<p>Cold War preparations to deter or to fight a third world war accelerated advances in <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technologies</a> that, though conceptualized before World War II, had been implemented for that war's exigencies, such as <a href="/wiki/Jet_aircraft" title="Jet aircraft">jet aircraft</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Scranton_312-0"><a href="#cite_note-Scranton-312">[306]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rocket" title="Rocket">rocketry</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-313"><a href="#cite_note-313">[307]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Computer" title="Computer">computers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENaughton20167_314-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENaughton20167-314">[308]</a></sup> In the decades after World War II, these advances led to jet travel;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Scranton_312-1"><a href="#cite_note-Scranton-312">[306]</a></sup> artificial satellites with innumerable applications,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b195_315-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b195-315">[309]</a></sup> including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GPS" title="GPS">GPS</a>;	
<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-316"><a href="#cite_note-316">[310]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b195_315-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b195-315">[309]</a></sup> which in the 1990s began to gain traction as a form of communication.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENaughton201614_317-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENaughton201614-317">[311]</a></sup> These inventions have revolutionized the movement of people, ideas, and information.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b195–6_318-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b195–6-318">[312]</a></sup>
</p><p>However, not all scientific and technological advances in the second half of the 20th century required an initial military impetus. That period also saw ground-breaking developments such as the discovery of the structure of <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPääbo200395_319-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPääbo200395-319">[313]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/DNA_sequencing" title="DNA sequencing">DNA sequencing</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPettersson_et_al.2009_320-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPettersson_et_al.2009-320">[314]</a></sup> the worldwide <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eradication_of_smallpox" title="Eradication of smallpox">eradication of smallpox</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a258_321-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a258-321">[315]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Green_Revolution" title="Green Revolution">Green Revolution</a> in agriculture,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a91_322-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a91-322">[316]</a></sup> the introduction of the portable <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone" title="Mobile phone">cellular phone</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a153_323-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a153-323">[317]</a></sup> the discovery of <a href="/wiki/Plate_tectonics" title="Plate tectonics">plate tectonics</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b200_324-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b200-324">[318]</a></sup> crewed and uncrewed <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">exploration of space</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b198_325-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b198-325">[319]</a></sup> and foundational discoveries in <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physics</a> phenomena ranging from the smallest entities (<a href="/wiki/Particle_physics" title="Particle physics">particle physics</a>) to the greatest entity (<a href="/wiki/Physical_cosmology" title="Physical cosmology">physical cosmology</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b200_324-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b200-324">[318]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/21st_century" title="21st century">21st century</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pudong_Shanghai_November_2017_panorama.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5100" data-file-width="10200" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Pudong_Shanghai_November_2017_panorama.jpg/330px-Pudong_Shanghai_November_2017_panorama.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Pudong_Shanghai_November_2017_panorama.jpg/495px-Pudong_Shanghai_November_2017_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Pudong_Shanghai_November_2017_panorama.jpg/660px-Pudong_Shanghai_November_2017_panorama.jpg 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pudong_Shanghai_November_2017_panorama.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> <a href="/wiki/Urbanization" title="Urbanization">urbanized</a> rapidly in the 21st century (pictured: <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>).</div></div></div><p>The 21st century has been marked by growing <a href="/wiki/Economic_globalization" title="Economic globalization">economic globalization</a> and integration,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedman2007137–138,_''passim''_326-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedman2007137–138,_''passim''-326">[320]</a></sup> with consequent increased risk to interlinked economies, as exemplified by the <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">Great Recession</a> of the late 2000s and early 2010s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a609_327-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a609-327">[321]</a></sup> This period has also seen the expansion of communications with <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphones</a> and the Internet, which have caused fundamental societal changes in business, politics, and individuals' personal lives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a153–154_328-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a153–154-328">[322]</a></sup>
</p><p>Humanity's impact on the Earth has risen due to growing populations and industrialization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a187_329-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a187-329">[323]</a></sup> The increased demands are contributing to <a href="/wiki/Environmental_degradation" title="Environmental degradation">environmental degradation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a71–77_330-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a71–77-330">[324]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcKibben2018_331-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcKibben2018-331">[325]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2020, the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> substantially disrupted global trading and caused recessions in the global economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAsareBarfi2021_332-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAsareBarfi2021-332">[326]</a></sup> As of 2022, more than <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_deaths" title="COVID-19 pandemic deaths">six million people</a> have died from <a href="/wiki/COVID-19" title="COVID-19">COVID-19</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERitchie_et_al._333-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERitchie_et_al.-333">[327]</a></sup>
</p>

</div><p><i><b><small><img alt="icon" class="noviewer" data-file-height="275" data-file-width="244" decoding="async" height="28" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Klepsydra-pt.svg/25px-Klepsydra-pt.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Klepsydra-pt.svg/37px-Klepsydra-pt.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Klepsydra-pt.svg/50px-Klepsydra-pt.svg.png 2x" width="25"/> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Modern_history" title="Portal:Modern history">Modern history portal</a></small></b></i> <i><b><small><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg"><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="3002" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="28" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg/28px-The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg/42px-The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg/56px-The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg 2x" width="28"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:World" title="Portal:World">World portal</a></small></b></i>
</p><h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Explanatory_notes">Explanatory notes</span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-columns references-column-width reflist-lower-alpha" style="column-width: 30em;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This date comes from the 2015 discovery of stone tools at the <a href="/wiki/Lomekwi" title="Lomekwi">Lomekwi</a> site in Kenya.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Some palaeontologists propose an earlier date of 3.39 million years ago based on bones found with butchery marks on them in <a href="/wiki/Dikika" title="Dikika">Dikika</a>, Ethiopia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> while others dispute both the Dikika and Lomekwi findings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-21">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Or perhaps earlier; the 2018 discovery of stone tools from 2.1 million years ago in <a href="/wiki/Shangchen" title="Shangchen">Shangchen</a>, China predates the earliest known <i>H. erectus</i> fossils.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-44"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-44">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">These dates come from a 2018 study of an upper jawbone from <a href="/wiki/Misliya_cave" title="Misliya cave">Misliya cave</a>, Israel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCI-20180126_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-SCI-20180126-41">[39]</a></sup> Researchers studying a fossil skull from <a href="/wiki/Apidima_Cave" title="Apidima Cave">Apidima Cave</a>, Greece in 2019 proposed an earlier date of 210,000 years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[40]</a></sup> The Apidima Cave study has been challenged by other scholars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-62"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-62">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This occurred during the <a href="/wiki/African_humid_period" title="African humid period">African humid period</a>, when the Sahara was much wetter than it is today.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarkerGoucher201559_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarkerGoucher201559-61">[58]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-249"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-249">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Early Modern," historically speaking, refers to Western European history from 1501 (after the widely accepted end of the <a href="/wiki/Late_Middle_Ages" title="Late Middle Ages">Late Middle Ages</a>; the transition period was the 15th century) to either 1750 or c. 1790–1800, by whichever <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Epoch_(reference_date)" title="Epoch (reference date)">epoch</a> is favoured by a school of scholars defining the period—which, in many cases of <a href="/wiki/Periodization" title="Periodization">periodization</a>, differs as well within a discipline such as art, philosophy or history.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-250"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-250">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Age of Enlightenment has also been referred to as the Age of Reason. Historians also include the late 17th century, which is typically known as the Age of Reason or Age of Rationalism, as part of the Enlightenment; however, contemporary historians have considered the Age of Reason distinct to the ideas developed in the Enlightenment. The use of the term here includes both Ages under a single all-inclusive time-frame.</span>
</li>
</ol></div>

<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEDunbar20168-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDunbar20168_6-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFDunbar2016">Dunbar 2016</a>, p. 8. "Conventionally, taxonomists now refer to the great ape family (including humans) as <i>hominids</i>, while all members of the lineage leading to modern humans that arose after the split with the [<i>Homo</i>-<i>Pan</i>] LCA are referred to as <i>hominins</i>. The older literature used the terms hominoids and hominids respectively."</span>

<li id="cite_note-Cela-Conde-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Cela-Conde_7-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Cela-Conde_7-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFCela-CondeAyala2003">Cela-Conde, C. <li id="cite_note-20"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-20">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFZhuDennellHuangWu2018">Zhu Z, Dennell R, Huang W, Wu Y, Qiu S, Yang S,  et al. (July 2018). "Hominin occupation of the Chinese Loess Plateau since about 2.1 million years ago". <i>Nature</i>. <b>559</b> (7715): 608–612. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bibcode_(identifier)" title="Bibcode (identifier)">Bibcode</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2018Natur.559..608Z" rel="nofollow">2018Natur.559..608Z</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1038%2Fs41586-018-0299-4" rel="nofollow">10.1038/s41586-018-0299-4</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/29995848" rel="nofollow">29995848</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S2CID_(identifier)" title="S2CID (identifier)">S2CID</a> <a class="external text" href="https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:49670311" rel="nofollow">49670311</a>. <q>Fourth, and most importantly, the oldest artefact age of approximately 2.12 Ma at Shangchen implies that hominins had left Africa before the date suggested by the earliest evidence from Dmanisi (about 1.85 Ma).
