<li id="cite_note-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-23">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFGowlett2016">Gowlett, J. A. J. (23 May 2016). <a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4874402" rel="nofollow">"The discovery of fire by humans: a long and convoluted process"</a>. <i>Philosophical Transactions of the Royal Society B: Biological Sciences</i>. <b>371</b> (1696): 20150164. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.1098%2Frstb.2015.0164" rel="nofollow">10.1098/rstb.2015.0164</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMC_(identifier)" title="PMC (identifier)">PMC</a> <span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely accessible"><a class="external text" href="//www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4874402" rel="nofollow">4874402</a></span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/27216521" rel="nofollow">27216521</a>. <q>We know that burning evidence occurs on numbers of archaeological sites from about 1.5 Ma onwards (there is evidence of actual hearths from around 0.7 to 0.4 Ma); that more elaborate technologies existed from around half a million years ago, and that these came to employ adhesives that require preparation by fire.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Philosophical+Transactions+of+the+Royal+Society+B%3A+Biological+Sciences&amp;rft.atitle=The+discovery+of+fire+by+humans%3A+a+long+and+convoluted+process&amp;rft.volume=371&amp;rft.issue=1696&amp;rft.pages=20150164&amp;rft.date=2016-05-23&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC4874402%23id-name%3DPMC&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F27216521&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1098%2Frstb.2015.0164&amp;rft.aulast=Gowlett&amp;rft.aufirst=J.+A.+J.&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC4874402&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHuman+history"></span></span>

</li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEChristian2015343–4-33"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChristian2015343–4_33-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFChristian2015">Christian 2015</a>, pp. 343–4. "Although the archaic human populations in most parts of Africa before around 70,000 BCE, in many aspects of their anatomies, appear almost modern, their cultural behaviors and their responses, for example to climatic challenge, reveal that they did not yet possess the full range of modern human capacities...The contrast with the capacities displayed by our fully modern human ancestors from 48,000 BCE onward could hardly be sharper."</span>
</li>

</li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEChristian2015316-50"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChristian2015316_50-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFChristian2015">Christian 2015</a>, p. 316. "Dispersal over an unprecedented swath of the globe...coincided with an Ice Age that...spread ice in the northern hemisphere as far south as the present lower courses of the Missouri and Ohio rivers in North America and deep into what are now the British Isles. Ice covered what is today Scandinavia. Most of the rest of what is now Europe was tundra or taiga. In central Eurasia, tundra reached almost to the present latitudes of the Black Sea. Steppe licked the shores of the Mediterranean. In the New World, tundra and taiga extended to where Virginia is today."</span>
</li>

href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/24757054" rel="nofollow">24757054</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=PNAS&amp;rft.atitle=Current+perspectives+and+the+future+of+domestication+studies&amp;rft.volume=111&amp;rft.issue=17&amp;rft.pages=6139-6146&amp;rft.date=2014&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC4035915%23id-name%3DPMC&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F24757054&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1073%2Fpnas.1323964111&amp;rft_id=info%3Abibcode%2F2014PNAS..111.6139L&amp;rft.aulast=Larson&amp;rft.aufirst=G.&amp;rft.au=Piperno%2C+D.+R.&amp;rft.au=Allaby%2C+R.+G.&amp;rft.au=Purugganan%2C+M.+D.&amp;rft.au=Andersson%2C+L.&amp;rft.au=Arroyo-Kalin%2C+M.&amp;rft.au=Barton%2C+L.&amp;rft.au=Climer+Vigueira%2C+C.&amp;rft.au=Denham%2C+T.&amp;rft.au=Dobney%2C+K.&amp;rft.au=Doust%2C+A.+N.&amp;rft.au=Gepts%2C+P.&amp;rft.au=Gilbert%2C+M.+T.+P.&amp;rft.au=Gremillion%2C+K.+J.&amp;rft.au=Lucas%2C+L.&amp;rft.au=Lukens%2C+L.&amp;rft.au=Marshall%2C+F.+B.&amp;rft.au=Olsen%2C+K.+M.&amp;rft.au=Pires%2C+J.C.&amp;rft.au=Richerson%2C+P.+J.&amp;rft.au=Rubio+De+Casas%2C+R.&amp;rft.au=Sanjur%2C+O.I.&amp;rft.au=Thomas%2C+M.+G.&amp;rft.au=Fuller%2C+D.Q.&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fpmc%2Farticles%2FPMC4035915&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHuman+history"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeill199911-58"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeill199911_58-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFMcNeill1999">McNeill 1999</a>, p. 11.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarkerGoucher2015325,_336-59"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarkerGoucher2015325,_336_59-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFBarkerGoucher2015">Barker &amp; Goucher 2015</a>, pp. 325, 336. "More recent improvements in archaeobotanical recovery have indicated that rice domestication was underway durin...the Hemudu cultural phase in the lower Yangtze valley...This points to a start of cultivation in this region of c. 10,000-9,000 years ago; in the middle Yangtze valley it could have begun someone earlier but may represent a parallel process to the lower Yangtze...it has been suggested on the basis of phytolith and starch residue evidence that broomcorn and foxtail millet were already in use in northern China prior to 7000 BCE. Nonetheless, the most abundant macrofossil evidence of broomcorn and foxtail millet is found in association with the early Neolithic sites post-7000 BCE."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarkerGoucher2015323-60"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarkerGoucher2015323_60-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFBarkerGoucher2015">Barker &amp; Goucher 2015</a>, p. 323.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarkerGoucher201559-61"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarkerGoucher201559_61-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFBarkerGoucher2015">Barker &amp; Goucher 2015</a>, p. 59.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.201521-63"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.201521_63-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.201521_63-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBulliet_et_al.201521_63-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFBulliet_et_al.2015">Bulliet et al. 2015</a>, p. 21.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarkerGoucher2015265-64"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarkerGoucher2015265_64-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFBarkerGoucher2015">Barker &amp; Goucher 2015</a>, p. 265.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarkerGoucher2015518-65"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarkerGoucher2015518_65-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFBarkerGoucher2015">Barker &amp; Goucher 2015</a>, p. 518. "Arrowroot was the earliest domesticate [in Panama], dating to 7800 BC at the Cueva de los Vampiros site and 5800 BCE at Aguadulce...Plant domestication began before 8500 BCE in southwest coastal Ecuador. Squash phytoliths were recovered from terminal Pleistocene and early Holocene strata at Vegas sites. Phytoliths recovered from the earliest levels are from wild squash, with domesticated size squash phytoliths directly dated to 9840–8555 BCE."</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEHourani19915,_11-178"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHourani19915,_11_178-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFHourani1991">Hourani 1991</a>, pp. 5, 11. "In the early seventh century a religious movement appeared on the margins of the great empires, those of the Byzantines and Sasanians, which dominated the western half of the world....The Byzantine and Sasanian empires were engaged in long wars, which lasted with intervals from 540 to 629."</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-kta_p113-239"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-kta_p113_239-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFThe_Association_of_Korean_History_Teachers2005">The Association of Korean History Teachers (2005). <i>Korea through the ages; Volume One: Ancient</i>. Seongnam-si: The Center for Information on Korean Culture, The Academy of Korean Studies. p. 113. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-89-7105-545-8" title="Special:BookSources/978-89-7105-545-8"><bdi>978-89-7105-545-8</bdi></a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Korea+through+the+ages%3B+Volume+One%3A+Ancient&amp;rft.place=Seongnam-si&amp;rft.pages=113&amp;rft.pub=The+Center+for+Information+on+Korean+Culture%2C+The+Academy+of+Korean+Studies&amp;rft.date=2005&amp;rft.isbn=978-89-7105-545-8&amp;rft.au=The+Association+of+Korean+History+Teachers&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHuman+history"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans_et_al.200714279-240"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans_et_al.200714279_240-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFEvans_et_al.2007">Evans et al. 2007</a>, p. 14279. "The 'boundary' of the urban complex of Angkor, as it can be loosely defined from the infrastructural network, encloses ~900–1,000 km² compared with the ~100–150 km² of Tikal, the next largest preindustrial low-density city for which we have an overall survey. Mirador, a Pre-Classic Maya urban complex, and Calakmul, a Classic site near Tikal, may be more extensive, but as yet we do not have comprehensive overall surveys for these sites; it is nonetheless clear that no site in the Maya world approaches Angkor in terms of extent."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTELieberman200391-241"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTELieberman200391_241-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFLieberman2003">Lieberman 2003</a>, p. 91.</span>

</li>

<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEPomeranz200031–32-282"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPomeranz200031–32_282-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFPomeranz2000">Pomeranz 2000</a>, pp. 31–32. "But in fact there is little evidence to suggest a quantitative advantage in Western Europe's capital stock before 1800 or a set of durable circumstances – demographic or otherwise – that gave Europe a significant edge in capital accumulation. Nor is it likely that Europeans were significantly healthier (i.e., advantaged in human capital), more productive, or otherwise heirs of many years of slowly accruing advantages over the more developed parts of Asia."</span>

<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcCormick1995155-306"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcCormick1995155_306-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFMcCormick1995">McCormick 1995</a>, p. 155.</span>

<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllison2018129–131-307"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllison2018129–131_307-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFAllison2018">Allison 2018</a>, p. 129–131. "As is now clear, the end of the Cold War produced a unipolar moment, not a unipolar era....When measured by the yardstick of purchasing power parity, the U.S. economy, which accounted for half of the world's GDP after World War II, had fallen to less than a quarter of global GDP by the end of the Cold War and stands at just one-seventh today."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrowning201816-308"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrowning201816_308-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFBrowning2018">Browning 2018</a>, p. 16. "In the first three postwar decades, workers and management effectively shared the increased wealth produced by the growth in <a href="/wiki/Productivity" title="Productivity">productivity</a>. Since the 1970s that <a href="/wiki/Social_contract" title="Social contract">social contract</a> has collapsed, <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">union</a> membership and influence have declined, wage growth has stagnated, and inequality in wealth has grown sharply."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEStiglitz2018-309"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStiglitz2018_309-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFStiglitz2018">Stiglitz 2018</a>. "By most accounts, the U.S. has the highest level of economic inequality among developed countries....Since the mid-1970s the rules of the economic game have been rewritten, both globally and nationally, in ways that advantage the rich and disadvantage the rest."</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a153-323"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a153_323-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFMcNeillPomeranz2015a">McNeill &amp; Pomeranz 2015a</a>, p. 153.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b200-324"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b200_324-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b200_324-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFMcNeillPomeranz2015b">McNeill &amp; Pomeranz 2015b</a>, p. 200.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b198-325"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015b198_325-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFMcNeillPomeranz2015b">McNeill &amp; Pomeranz 2015b</a>, p. 198.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEFriedman2007137–138,_''passim''-326"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFriedman2007137–138,_''passim''_326-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFFriedman2007">Friedman 2007</a>, pp. 137–138, <i>passim</i>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a609-327"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a609_327-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFMcNeillPomeranz2015a">McNeill &amp; Pomeranz 2015a</a>, p. 609. "But the crisis beginning in 2007, with the eddying effects of the subprime lending-induced financial crash, demonstrated how vital the health of the American economy remained for global growth and stability. Events and processes outside the United States continued to affect the internal politics and economics, and vice versa. The United States and the rest of the world were interconnected, and disengagement was impossible."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a153–154-328"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a153–154_328-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFMcNeillPomeranz2015a">McNeill &amp; Pomeranz 2015a</a>, pp. 153–154.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a187-329"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a187_329-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFMcNeillPomeranz2015a">McNeill &amp; Pomeranz 2015a</a>, p. 187.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a71–77-330"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNeillPomeranz2015a71–77_330-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFMcNeillPomeranz2015a">McNeill &amp; Pomeranz 2015a</a>, pp. 71–77.</span>
</li>

</li>
